Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introducing Usul al-Bazdawi: A Foundational Hanafi Usul Text
Book title, author, commentator, and publisher details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and full title of Usul al-Bazdawi and explain its significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi systematically presents Hanafi principles of legal interpretation.

Even a title page carries weight. This lesson decodes the front matter of one of the most important Hanafi usul works. You will learn how to identify a classical text's author, commentator, and scholarly lineage—skills essential for navigating any madrasa text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main text and author
Locate the title and author's name. The title is 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul', commonly known as 'Usul al-Bazdawi'. The author is Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi.
The author's honorific 'Fakhr al-Islam' indicates his high standing.
2
Note the companion work and commentator
The edition includes 'Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi' by Imām Qāsim ibn Qutlubughā al-Hanafi. This work traces the hadith evidence cited by al-Bazdawi.
Takhrij works verify the sources of hadith, a crucial step in usul study.
3
Examine the editor and publisher
The edition is edited by Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash and published by Dar al-Sharq al-Islamiyya. This gives you the scholarly chain of transmission (isnad) for this printed edition.
Knowing the editor and publisher helps assess the reliability of the print.
4
Understand the work's place in Hanafi usul
Al-Bazdawi's text is one of the three foundational usul works in the Hanafi school (alongside Usul al-Karkhi and Usul al-Sarakhsi). It is known for its clarity and systematic structure.
This makes the text a key reference for students of Hanafi methodology.

Source Text

(400-5482) رحمه الله تعالى

Usul al-Bazdawi: Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul. By Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi (d. 400-5482? - may Allah have mercy on him). Accompanied by: Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi by the Imam, the all-knowing Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi (d. 5879-882 - may Allah have mercy on him). Edited by Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. Dar al-Sharq al-Islamiyya (802-5879).
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book. It identifies the main work as 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul' (The Treasure of Attaining Knowledge of the Principles) by Imam Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi. Al-Bazdawi's work is a foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, known for its systematic presentation of the Hanafi methodological principles. The edition also includes a commentary called 'Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi' by Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi, which traces the hadith references used by al-Bazdawi. The book is published by Dar al-Sharq al-Islamiyya and edited by Dr. Sa'id Bakdash.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The title of the work; a classical manual of Hanafi usul al-fiqh by Imam al-Bazdawi.
كنز الوصول إلى معرفة الأصول (Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul): The full title of the book, meaning 'The Treasure of Attaining Knowledge of the Principles'.
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Honorific title of Imam al-Bazdawi, meaning 'Pride of Islam'.
تخريج (Takhrij): The process of tracing hadith back to their original sources and verifying their chain of transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of the main work 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul'?
A) Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
B) Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi
C) Dr. Sa'id Bakdash
D) Dar al-Sharq al-Islamiyya

Key Takeaway
This title page identifies Usul al-Bazdawi as a foundational Hanafi usul text, accompanied by a hadith takhrij, and published in a critical edition.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Significance of Kanz al-Wusul: Al-Bazdawi's Foundational Text on Hanafi Usul
Opening title page of a Hanafi usul textbook.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the full title and author of Kanz al-Wusul and explain its importance in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
Kanz al-Wusul is the classic Hanafi usul text by Imam al-Bazdawi, essential for understanding Hanafi legal theory.

This opening page introduces us to one of the most important works in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul by Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali b. Muhammad al-Bazdawi. This text, commonly known as Usul al-Bazdawi, has been a core reference for Hanafi jurists for centuries. Alongside it, the edition includes the takhrij of hadith by Qasim b. Qutlubugha, a later Hanafi scholar. Understanding the author and the work's place in the tradition is the first step in mastering Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full title of the work
The full Arabic title is 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul', but it is commonly abbreviated as 'Usul al-Bazdawi'.
Note the distinction: full title vs. common name.
2
Identify the author and his full name
The author is Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali b. Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi.
His death date is 482 AH, though the OCR shows corrupted numbers.
3
Recognize the accompanying work
The edition includes 'Takhrīj Aḥādīth Uṣūl al-Bazdawī' by Imam Qasim b. Qutlubugha al-Hanafi.
Takhrij refers to the verification and sourcing of hadith used in the original text.
4
Understand the significance in Hanafi usul
Kanz al-Wusul is a foundational text that systematically presents Hanafi principles of jurisprudence, later commented upon by many scholars.
It is considered one of the 'Usul al-Hanafiyya' pillars.

Source Text

Actually d. 482/1089) may Allah have mercy on him. With it: Takhrīj Aḥādīth Uṣūl al-Bazdawī by Imam al-Allamah Qasim bin Qutlubugha al-Hanafi (d. 802/1399 or 587? Commentary
This is the title page of the book 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul' by Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali b. Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi, one of the foundational texts in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The work is also known as 'Usul al-Bazdawi'. The text includes mention of the takhrij (verification of hadith) by Imam Qasim b. Qutlubugha, a later Hanafi scholar, and the editor of this edition, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. The page is repeated with slight variations, likely due to a formatting issue in the scan.

Key Terms
كنز الوصول إلى معرفة الأصول (Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul): Title of the work: 'The Treasure of Access to Knowledge of the Principles'
تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي (Takhrīj Aḥādīth Uṣūl al-Bazdawī): The verification of hadith referenced in Usul al-Bazdawi, done by Qasim b. Qutlubugha

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Science of Usul al-Fiqh: The Scale of Sharia
Editor's introduction praising the science of Usul al-Fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the essential role of Usul al-Fiqh in preserving the integrity of Islamic law and distinguish between qualified and unqualified claims of ijtihad.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is the gatekeeper of ijtihad—it protects Sharia from distortion and enables qualified scholars.

The editor of this classical Hanafi text opens with a powerful praise of Usul al-Fiqh, describing it as a noble science that regulates and protects the rulings of Sharia. He warns against the dangers of unqualified people issuing fatwas, while simultaneously highlighting how this discipline illuminates the path for serious students. In this lesson, we will unpack these key themes to appreciate why Usul al-Fiqh is indispensable for anyone studying the Hanafi legal tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's praise of Usul al-Fiqh
Read the opening lines to see how the editor describes Usul al-Fiqh as a 'noble science' (min al-'ulum al-jalilah). Note the specific functions he attributes to it.
Focus on the terms: 'regulating rulings', 'preserving from tampering'.
2
Understand its protective function
The editor says Usul al-Fiqh 'closed the doors of ijtihad before every ignorant claimant'. This means it acts as a filter to prevent unqualified individuals from distorting the religion.
Contrast with the idea that anyone can derive rulings without training.
3
Recognize the danger of unqualified fatwa
The passage mentions 'the audacity of those who dare to give fatwas... without knowledge'. Reflect on the harm that results from uninformed legal opinions.
Think of modern examples where people claim to speak for Islam without proper credentials.
4
Appreciate the enabling role for scholars
The editor also emphasizes that Usul al-Fiqh 'illuminated the path for students of knowledge'. It is not just restrictive; it provides a clear methodology for qualified scholars to derive correct rulings.
The science is both a shield and a lamp.
5
Summarize the dual function
Usul al-Fiqh protects the Sharia from distortion and provides a systematic method for derivation. This is why it is called a 'scale' (mizan) for the imams.
This duality is key to understanding the discipline's importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المحقق
الحمد لله رب العالمين، وأفضل الصلاة وأكمل التسليم على سيدنا محمد سيد الأولين والآخرين، ورضي الله عن آله وأصحابه أجمعين، ومن تبعهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين، وعن ورثة النبوة العاملين من فحول الفقهاء والأصوليين والأئمة المدققين، ومن أقامهم الله لتثبيت هذا الدين، ونصرة الحق المبين، وأعدهم وأمدهم بما تحار به عقول المفكرين، وارض عنا معهم بفضلك وكرمك وإحسانك يا رب العالمين.
وبعد: فإن علم أصول الفقه من العلوم الجليلة، الذي كان له الحظ الأوفر في ضبط أحكام الشريعة وحفظها من عبث العابثين، وتأويل الجاهلين، وجرأة المتجرئين على الفتيا، والمتطفلين بغير علم، ويحسبون أنهم يعلمون. وهو العلم الذي أوصد أبواب الاجتهاد والترجيح أمام كل مدع جاهل وحال دون دخول هذا الصرح العلمي الشامخ كل متطاول وأوقف الناس عند حدودهم، وعرفهم قدرهم وحالهم. وفي الوقت نفسه فهو العلم الذي أنار الطريق لطلاب العلم من أصحاب القدرات العلمية، والملكة الفقهية للنظر في أحكام دينه المنيف، وتبيين شرعه الحنيف. وهو الميزان الذي يعرف به كيف استنبط الأئمة الفقهاء الفروع و...
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The editor's introduction. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and the best of prayers and complete peace be upon our master Muhammad, the master of the first and the last, and may Allah be pleased with his family and all his companions, and those who follow them with excellence until the Day of Judgment, and concerning the inheritors of prophethood, the workers among the great jurists, usul scholars, and precise imams, and those whom Allah established to solidify this religion and support the clear truth, and He prepared them and provided them with what leaves the minds of thinkers bewildered, and be pleased with us along with them by Your bounty, generosity, and kindness, O Lord of the worlds. To proceed: Indeed, the science of Usul al-Fiqh is among the noble sciences, which had the greatest fortune in regulating the rulings of Sharia and preserving them from the tampering of the tamperers, and the interpretation of the ignorant, and the audacity of those who dare to give fatwas, and the intruders without knowledge, thinking that they know. It is the science that closed the doors of ijtihad and tarjih before every ignorant claimant and prevented every overstepper from entering this lofty scholarly edifice, and stopped people at their limits, and made them know their worth and status. At the same time, it is the science that illuminated the path for students of knowledge with scientific abilities and juristic discernment to examine the rulings of His noble religion and clarify His pure law. It is the scale by which it is known how the imams and jurists derived the branches and...
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the book, praising the science of Usul al-Fiqh. The editor begins with the basmalah and praises Allah and sends blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad and his companions. He then praises the scholars, especially the jurists and usul scholars, as inheritors of the prophets. He emphasizes that Usul al-Fiqh is a noble science that protects the Sharia from distortion by the ignorant and those who issue fatwas without knowledge. It closes the door to false claims of ijtihad and prevents unqualified individuals from engaging in legal interpretation. At the same time, it provides a clear path for qualified students to derive rulings. The editor describes Usul al-Fiqh as a scale (mizan) that shows how the imams derived subsidiary rulings. This introduction sets the stage for the technical content to follow, highlighting the importance and authority of the discipline.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The science of the foundations of Islamic jurisprudence, which provides the methodology for deriving legal rulings from the primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the editor, what is the primary function of the science of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) To provide direct fatwas for everyday issues.
B) To regulate and protect the rulings of Sharia from distortion and misapplication.
C) To critique the opinions of the early jurists.
D) To derive new rulings without any methodology.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is the indispensable methodology that both safeguards the Sharia from corruption and empowers qualified scholars to derive rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Introduction to Usul al-Bazdawi: A Foundational Hanafi Usul Work
Editor's introduction praising the book and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of Usul al-Bazdawi and explain its significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi is the preeminent Hanafi usul work, balancing conciseness with thorough proofs.

This lesson introduces you to one of the most important books in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Usul al-Bazdawi. The editor's preface offers a window into the book's stature, its author's credentials, and why it demands deep study. You will learn about the author, the book's method, and how it fits into the larger tradition of Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and author
The passage introduces Usul al-Bazdawi by its full title and author: Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH). Note his full name, birth/death years, and his other major works (e.g., a 120-volume tafsir and al-Mabsut).
The author is also known as Abu al-Usr al-Bazdawi.
2
Understand the book's purpose
According to the author's own statement, the book aims 'to explain the texts with their meanings, and to define the principles by their branches on the condition of brevity and conciseness.' This tells you the book is both concise and comprehensive.
Conciseness (ijaz) is a hallmark of the text.
3
Analyze the commentary by Alauddin al-Bukhari
The editor quotes al-Bukhari's praise from Kashf al-Asrar. Al-Bukhari highlights the book's excellent arrangement, lofty status, and difficulty. Only a scholar fully devoted and already well-versed in fiqh can master it.
This indicates that Usul al-Bazdawi is not a beginner's text; it assumes prior knowledge.
4
Recognize the need for a critical edition
The editor laments that the book had not received proper scholarly service and was printed in faulty editions. He explains his methodology: relying on ten manuscripts, the oldest from 651 AH, to produce a reliable text.
Understanding the textual history is important for usul scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأحكام، وبه يوقف على القواعد والأصول التي أقام بناءَها أهلُ الذِّكر على أُسس راسخة، وحُجَج دامغة، وكيف ساروا عليها؛ ليكون اللاحقون على قدم العلماء السابقين وهديهم القويم، حتى لا تَزِلُّ أقلامهم وأحكامهم، فإن زَلَّة العالم زلَّةُ العالم، اللهم سلّمنا وسلّم منا. وإن من كتب الإسلام العظيمة النفيسة المعتبرة المعتمدة المشتهرة في علم أصول الفقه على طريقة فقهاء السادة الحنفية: كتاب فخرِ الإسلام البَزْدَوِيَّ، أستاذ الأئمة، الإمام الكبير ببلاد ما وراء النهر، الفقيه الأصولي المحدِّثِ المفسِّرِ أبي العُسر علي بن محمدِ البَزْدَوِي، المولودِ في حدود سنة ٤٠٠ هـ، والمتوفى سنة ٤٨٢هـ، رحمه الله، صاحب المصنفات العالية البارعة الدقيقة النافعة، والتي منها تفسير للقرآن الكريم في (۱۲۰) مجلداً، والمبسوط في فروع الفقه الحنفي، في أحد عشر مجلداً. وقد جاء كتاب أصول البزدوي لبيان النصوص بمعانيها، وتعريف الأصول بفروعها على شرط الإيجاز والاختصار»، كما قال مؤلفه رحمه الله في مقدمته. وهو كتاب عظيم الشأن جليل البرهان، محتو على لطائف الاعتبارات، بأوجز العبارات، ويمتاز بأمر مهم جداً، وهو التدليل للقواعد الأصولية، وطُرُقِ استنباط الأحكام عند الحنفية، من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والشواهد اللغوية مع تطبيق ذلك على أمثلة كثيرة من الفروع الفقهية، وهذا أمر مهم جداً يتطلَّع إليه كل فقيه أصولي محقق مدقق، ويسعى إليه كلُّ مَن دَرَس الفقه المقارن بين المذاهب الفقهية بدقة، أو درسه بحنكة. وقد وَصَفَ كتاب «أصول البزدوي شارحه الإمام علاء الدين البخاري الحنفي (ت ٧٣٠هـ) في مقدمة كشف الأسرار، وأثنى عليه، وبين حاله، وعلو مقامه بقوله: امتاز أصول البزدوي من بين الكتب المصنفة في هذا الفنّ شَرَفاً وسُمُواً، وحل محلَّه مَقامَ الثّريَّا مَجْداً وعُلواً، ضمن فيه أصول الشرع وأحكامه، وأدرج فيه ما به نظام الفقه وقوامه. وهو كتاب عجيب الصَّنْعة رائع الترتيب صحيح الأسلوب مليحُ التركيب، ليس في جَوْدة تركيبه وحُسن ترتيبه مرية، وليس وراء عبادان قرية، لكنه صَعْبُ المَرام، أَبِيُّ الزَّمام، لا سبيل إلى الوصول إلى معرفة لُطفه وغرائبه، ولا طريق إلى الإحاطة بطرقه وعجائبه إلا لمن أقبل بكليته على تحقيقه وتحصيله، وشدَّ حَيَازيمه بالإحاطة بجملته وتفصيله، بعد أن رزق في اقتباس العلم ذهناً جَلِيّاً، وذَرْعاً من هواجس أضاليل المنى خليّاً، وقد تبحر مع ذلك في الأحكام والفروع، وأحاط بما جاء فيها من المنقول والمسموع». اهـ وهكذا قدر الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب العظيم أنه إلى الآن لم ينل حظه من الخدمة العلمية التي تليق بمقامه العالي الرفيع، ولم يُطبع مفرداً إلا طبعات تجاريةً سقيمةً عليلة، بل مع أسقاط في مواضع عديدة، وكذلك حال طبعاته التي جاءت مع شروحه القديمة والحديثة، وقد أكرمني الله تعالى ويسر لي تحقيقه، وأعانني على خدمته، معتمداً على عَشْرِ نُسَخ خطية نفيسة، أقدمها بتاريخ سنة ٦٥١هـ، والحمد الله على جوده وإحسانه. ومما زادني ربي من فضله وكرمه: أن يسر لي أيضاً تحقيق وخدمة كتاب: تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي»، للإمام المحدث الحافظ الفقيه
And the rulings, and by it one comes to know the foundations and principles upon which the people of remembrance built their structure on firm bases, conclusive proofs, and how they proceeded upon them; so that those who come later may follow in the footsteps of the earlier scholars and their straight guidance, so that their pens and rulings do not slip, for the slip of a scholar is the slip of the world. O Allah, keep us safe and protect us. Among the great, valuable, esteemed, relied-upon, and famous Islamic books in the science of Usul al-Fiqh according to the method of the Hanafi jurists is the book of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, the teacher of the imams, the great imam in Transoxiana, the jurist, usuli, muhaddith, mufassir Abu al-Usr Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, born around 400 AH and died in 482 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, the author of excellent, brilliant, precise, and beneficial works, among which is a commentary on the Holy Qur'an in 120 volumes, and al-Mabsut in the branches of Hanafi fiqh in eleven volumes. The book Usul al-Bazdawi came to explain the texts with their meanings, and to define the principles by their branches on the condition of brevity and conciseness, as its author said in his introduction. It is a great book, of magnificent proof, containing subtle considerations in the briefest expressions, and it is distinguished by a very important matter, namely the evidence for usul principles and the methods of deriving rulings according to the Hanafis from the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and linguistic evidence, with application of that to many examples of fiqh branches. This is a very important matter that every investigating and precise usuli jurist aspires to, and everyone who has studied comparative fiqh between madhhabs accurately or studied it with wisdom seeks it. The commentator Imam Alauddin al-Bukhari al-Hanafi (d. 730 AH) described the book Usul al-Bazdawi in the introduction of Kashf al-Asrar, praised it, explained its condition and high status, saying: 'Usul al-Bazdawi stands out among the books written in this art in honor and loftiness, and has taken the place of the Pleiades in glory and highness. It encompasses the principles of Shari'ah and its rulings, and includes that which establishes the system of fiqh and its strength. It is a book of wondrous construction, splendid arrangement, correct style, beautiful composition. There is no doubt about the quality of its composition and good arrangement, and there is no village beyond Abadan. But it is difficult of attainment, refractory to control. There is no way to reach knowledge of its subtleties and wonders, nor any path to encompass its methods and marvels, except for one who devotes himself entirely to its verification and acquisition, and tightens his belt to encompass its totality and detail, after having been granted a clear mind in acquiring knowledge, and a heart free from the obsessions of false hopes, and having become deeply versed in rulings and branches, and encompassed what has come in them of transmitted and heard reports.' So it is. Thus Allah decreed that this great book has not yet received its share of scholarly service befitting its high and lofty status, and it has not been printed alone except in faulty, weak commercial editions, even with omissions in many places, and likewise with its editions that came with its old and modern commentaries. Allah has honored me and facilitated its verification, and helped me to serve it, relying on ten precious manuscript copies, the oldest dated 651 AH. Praise be to Allah for His bounty and beneficence. Among what my Lord has increased me from His bounty and generosity is that He also facilitated the verification and service of the book Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi by the imam, muhaddith, hafiz, faqih
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the book Usul al-Bazdawi, a foundational work in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The editor begins by highlighting the importance of understanding the principles and proofs upon which earlier scholars built their rulings, so that later scholars may follow their path without error. He then introduces the author, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, giving his full name, approximate birth date (400 AH), death date (482 AH), and listing some of his major works, including a massive tafsir in 120 volumes and al-Mabsut in fiqh. The editor notes that Usul al-Bazdawi was written to explain texts and principles concisely, and praises its comprehensiveness and evidentiary approach. He quotes the commentator and scholar Alauddin al-Bukhari's detailed praise from his supercommentary Kashf al-Asrar, which emphasizes the book's lofty status, excellent composition, and difficulty. Al-Bukhari states that only a dedicated, insightful scholar who is well-versed in fiqh can fully grasp its subtleties. Finally, the editor laments that the book has not received proper scholarly attention and has been printed in faulty editions, and he describes his own work in producing a critical edition based on ten manuscripts, the oldest from 651 AH. He also mentions his work on a companion volume on the hadith evidence for the book.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The name of the book by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi on Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
فقهاء السادة الحنفية (Fuqaha' al-sadah al-Hanafiyyah): The Hanafi jurists, the school of thought followed in this book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A commentary on the Quran in 120 volumes
B) Al-Mabsut in fiqh in eleven volumes

D) Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Bazdawi is a concise yet comprehensive Hanafi usul text, praised for its proofs and method, but demanding deep prior knowledge.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Significance and Difficulty of Usul al-Bazdawi
Editorial introduction quoting praise and describing the book's challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the reputation of Usul al-Bazdawi as praised by al-Bukhari al-Hanafi and explain why it is considered a difficult yet foundational work in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi is a masterpiece of Hanafi usul, but its depth demands full devotion to master.

Usul al-Bazdawi is a cornerstone of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. In his introduction, the editor quotes a glowing description from al-Bukhari al-Hanafi, highlighting the book's lofty status, perfect composition, and formidable difficulty. This lesson unpacks that description and sets the stage for understanding why this work commands such respect in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the praise of al-Bukhari
Identify the key phrases used by al-Bukhari al-Hanafi to describe Usul al-Bazdawi: 'distinguished among books', 'occupies the place of Pleiades', 'wondrous composition', 'difficult to reach'. What do these metaphors convey about the book's status?
Focus on the metaphor 'no village beyond Abadan' — meaning nothing compares to it after a certain point.
2
Identify the conditions for mastery
According to al-Bukhari, what is required to master this book? Note the phrases: 'devotes himself entirely to its verification', 'tightens his resolve', 'clear mind', 'heart free from false hopes', 'deeply versed in rulings and branches'.
This shows the high level of prerequisite knowledge and effort needed.
3
Connect to the Hanafi usul tradition
Consider why such a difficult text is important in Hanafi usul. Usul al-Bazdawi is a key text in the Hanafi madrasa tradition, often studied after simpler works. Its difficulty reflects the depth of Hanafi legal theory.
Think of it as an advanced text that builds on earlier primers.

قال البخاري الحنفي (ت ٧٣٠هـ) في مقدمة كشف الأسرار، وأثنى عليه، وبين حاله، وعلو مقامه بقوله : لله امتاز أصول البزدوي من بين الكتب المصنفة في هذا الفنّ شَرَفاً وسُمُواً، وحل محلَّه مَقامَ الثّريَّا مَجْداً وعُلواً، ضمن فيه أصول الشرع وأحكامه، وأدرج فيه ما به نظام الفقه وقوامه. وهو كتاب عجيب الصَّنْعة رائع الترتيب صحيح الأسلوب مليحُ التركيب، ليس في جَوْدة تركيبه وحُسن ترتيبه مرية، وليس وراء عبادان قرية، لكنه صَعْبُ المَرام، أَبِيُّ الزَّمام، لا سبيل إلى الوصول إلى معرفة لُطفه وغرائبه، ولا طريق إلى الإحاطة بطرقه وعجائبه إلا لمن أقبل بكليته على تحقيقه وتحصيله، وشدَّ حَيَازيمه بالإحاطة بجملته وتفصيله، بعد أن رزق في اقتباس العلم ذهناً جَلِيّاً، وذَرْعاً من هواجس أضاليل المنى خليّاً، وقد تبحر مع ذلك في الأحكام والفروع ، وأحاط بما جاء فيها من المنقول والمسموع». اهـ وهكذا قدر الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب العظيم أنه إلى الآن لم ينل حظه من الخدمة العلمية التي تليق بمقامه العالي الرفيع، ولم يُطبع مفرداً إلا طبعات تجاريةً سقيمةً عليلة، بل مع أسقاط في مواضع عديدة، وكذلك حال طبعاته التي جاءت مع شروحه القديمة والحديثة، وقد أكرمني الله تعالى ويسر لي تحقيقه، وأعانني على خدمته، معتمداً على عَشْرِ نُسَخ خطية نفيسة، أقدمها بتاريخ سنة ٦٥١هـ ، والحمد الله على جوده وإحسانه. لكن كَم الكريم من عاداته يولي الضعيف فضله ويمنح ومما زادني ربي من فضله وكرمه : أن يسر لي أيضاً تحقيق وخدمة كتاب: تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي»، للإمام المحدث الحافظ الفقيه الأصولي المفنّن في علوم كثيرة، المحقق المدقق البارع العلامة قاسم بن قُطلوبغا، المتوفى سنة ٨٧٩هـ، وذلك على نسختين: نسخة المؤلف بخطه، ونسخة بخط تلميذه، وقد قرأها عليه وأجازه بها بخطه. ولم ينشغل العلامةُ قاسم وهو في خِضَمَ تخريجه لأحاديث الكتاب وآثاره واستدلاله لمسائل عديدة عن تسجيل بعض الاستدراكات الأصولية، والملاحظات الاستدلالية على صاحب الكتاب مع إمامته الكبرى. وهكذا جمعت بين الكتابين الأصولي والحديثي في دفتي مجلد واحد، وأنزلتُ تخريج كل حديث وأثر في مكانه من أصول البزدوي، والتقى الفرع بالأصل، وتم ولله الحمد جَمْعُ الشمل. وكان من منهجي في إخراج كتاب أصول البزدوي وقصدي الأول: الاجتهاد والسعي لإثبات نص صحيح للكتاب من خلال النُّسَخ الخطية مع مراجعة الشروح، دون التعليق عليه ؛ لأن إيضاح مُغلَقاته وشرحها يحتاج إلى جُمَل وسطورٍ يَضيق المقام عنها، ومن أراد الوقوف على طلبته، وتحصيل بغيته : فشروحه متوافرة بكل يسر. هذا، وقد اجتهدت في تقديمه للقراء الكرام بحُلَّةٍ مُشرِقةٍ تَسرُّ الناظرين، مع القيام بتفقير نصه ومسائله ، ووضع علامات الترقيم، وضَبْطِ ما أشكل من ألفاظه، وقدمت له بترجمة للإمام البزدوي بحسب الوسع والطاقة مع دراسة عن الكتاب بتحقيق اسمه وذكر شروحه، وبيان منهجه وجمع مزاياه وثناء العلماء عليه. كما عملت مقارنةً بينه وبين أصول عصريه الإمام السرخسي، والتي تبين لي من خلالها مبدئياً أن أصول السرخسي بمثابة شرح له، والله أعلم. وهكذا سِرْتُ على هذا المنوال أيضاً في خدمة كتاب تخريج أحاديثه
Al-Bukhari al-Hanafi (d. 730 AH) said in the introduction to Kashf al-Asrar, praising it and describing its status and lofty position: 'By Allah, Usul al-Bazdawi is distinguished among books written in this discipline in honor and sublimity, and it occupies the place of Pleiades in glory and loftiness. It contains the principles of Sharia and its rulings, and incorporates that by which the system and strength of fiqh is established. It is a book of wondrous composition, magnificent arrangement, correct style, and beautiful structure. There is no doubt about the excellence of its composition and the beauty of its arrangement; there is no village beyond Abadan. But it is difficult to reach, stubborn in control; there is no way to attain knowledge of its subtleties and marvels, nor any path to encompass its paths and wonders, except for one who devotes himself entirely to its verification and acquisition, and tightens his resolve to encompass its entirety and detail, after being granted a clear mind for acquiring knowledge and a heart free from the whispers of false hopes, and who is deeply versed in rulings and branches, and encompasses what has been transmitted and heard in them.' End quote. Thus Allah decreed for this great book that until now it has not received its share of scholarly service befitting its high and lofty status. It has not been printed individually except in defective commercial editions, with omissions in many places, and likewise the editions that came with its old and modern commentaries. Allah has honored me and facilitated its verification, and helped me serve it, relying on ten precious manuscript copies, the oldest dated 651 AH. Praise be to Allah for His bounty and kindness. But the generous one's habit is to bestow favor on the weak and grant. And among the additional favors of my Lord is that He facilitated for me also the verification and service of the book 'Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi' by the imam, muhaddith, hafiz, faqih, usuli, versatile in many sciences, the verifier, precise, brilliant scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, d. 879 AH, based on two copies: the author's copy in his own hand, and a copy in the hand of his student, who read it to him and he authorized him with it in his handwriting. And the scholar Qasim, while engaged in his takhrij of the book's hadiths and reports and his deduction of many issues, did not neglect to record some usul corrections and evidentiary observations regarding the author despite his great imamate. Thus I combined the two books - the usul and the hadith - in one volume, and placed the takhrij of each hadith and report in its place in Usul al-Bazdawi, uniting the branch with the root, and by Allah's grace the collection was completed. My methodology in producing Usul al-Bazdawi and my primary intention was: to strive and endeavor to establish a sound text of the book from the manuscript copies while consulting the commentaries, without commentary; because explaining its obscure points and commentary would require many lines and sentences beyond the scope here, and whoever wants to pursue its demands and attain his desire: its commentaries are readily available. This, and I have endeavored to present it to the esteemed readers in a bright garment pleasing to the eye, while dividing its text and issues, adding punctuation, correcting problematic words, and prefacing it with a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi to the extent possible, along with a study of the book investigating its name, mentioning its commentaries, explaining its methodology, collecting its merits, and scholars' praise for it. I also made a comparison between it and the Usul of his contemporary Imam al-Sarakhsi, from which it became apparent to me initially that Usul al-Sarakhsi is like a commentary on it. Allah knows best. And I proceeded in this manner also in serving the book of Takhrij of its hadiths.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to his critical edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul (Kanz al-Wusul). He begins by quoting al-Bukhari al-Hanafi's praise from his commentary Kashf al-Asrar, emphasizing the book's high rank, unique style, and difficulty. The editor then laments the lack of proper scholarly edition, noting that previous prints had omissions. He explains his methodology: he used ten manuscripts, the oldest from 651 AH, to establish a sound text without adding commentary, as many commentaries already exist. He also included a companion work, Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi by Ibn Qutlubugha, reconciling the two. Additionally, he provides a biography of al-Bazdawi, a study of the book's name and commentaries, and a comparison with al-Sarakhsi's Usul. The focus is on editorial procedure, not on teaching usul al-fiqh content.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): A foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh work by Imam al-Bazdawi, known for its depth and difficulty.
كشف الأسرار (Kashf al-Asrar): A commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi by al-Bukhari al-Hanafi (d. 730 AH).
ثريا (Thurayya): Pleiades star cluster, used metaphorically to indicate high status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Editor's Methodology: Critical Edition and Integration
Editor explains his methodology for the critical edition and integration with takhrij.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the editor's methodology for establishing the text of Usul al-Bazdawi and explain how he integrated Ibn Qutlubugha's hadith takhrij.

Core Idea
A critical edition of Usul al-Bazdawi needs multiple manuscripts and the companion takhrij to be fully serviceable.

The editor details his scholarly approach: using ten manuscript copies, with the oldest from 651 AH, to produce a reliable text. He also includes a companion work, Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi by Ibn Qutlubugha, placing each hadith takhrij in its proper place. This lesson explores the editorial decisions and their significance for Hanafi usul scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual resources used
List the primary resources the editor used: ten manuscript copies, the oldest from 651 AH. Also note the use of two manuscript copies for the takhrij (author's copy and student's copy).
Why is the oldest manuscript (651 AH) significant? It is relatively early, close to the author's time (al-Bazdawi died 482 AH).
2
Understand the editor's primary goal
The editor states his 'primary intention' was to establish a sound text from the manuscripts, without adding commentary. Why? He says explaining obscure points 'would require many lines' and commentaries are already available.
This is a standard approach for critical editions: focus on the text, not interpretation.
3
Analyze the integration of the takhrij
The editor combined Usul al-Bazdawi with Ibn Qutlubugha's takhrij (hadith verification) in one volume. Each hadith or athar is placed in its corresponding location in the main text. This 'uniting the branch with the root' aims to provide immediate evidence.
Think about why this integration is valuable: it saves the reader from flipping between two books.
4
Assess the added scholarly apparatus
The editor also added a biography of al-Bazdawi, a study of the book's name and commentaries, and a comparison with al-Sarakhsi's Usul. What purpose do these additions serve?
These provide context and show the scholarly network around the text.
5
Reflect on the value of this methodology
How does this editorial work benefit modern research? Reliable text, accessible evidence, and contextual studies facilitate deeper study of Hanafi usul.
The editor mentions he did not comment on the text because the commentaries are available, trusting that users will use them.

للقراء الكرام بحُلَّةٍ مُشرِقةٍ تَسرُّ الناظرين، مع القيام بتفقير نصه ومسائله ، ووضع علامات الترقيم، وضَبْطِ ما أشكل من ألفاظه، وقدمت له بترجمة للإمام البزدوي بحسب الوسع والطاقة مع دراسة عن الكتاب بتحقيق اسمه وذكر شروحه، وبيان منهجه وجمع مزاياه وثناء العلماء عليه. كما عملت مقارنةً بينه وبين أصول عصريه الإمام السرخسي، والتي تبين لي من خلالها مبدئياً أن أصول السرخسي بمثابة شرح له، والله أعلم. وهكذا سِرْتُ على هذا المنوال أيضاً في خدمة كتاب تخريج أحاديثه
Al-Bukhari al-Hanafi (d. 730 AH) said in the introduction to Kashf al-Asrar, praising it and describing its status and lofty position: 'By Allah, Usul al-Bazdawi is distinguished among books written in this discipline in honor and sublimity, and it occupies the place of Pleiades in glory and loftiness. It contains the principles of Sharia and its rulings, and incorporates that by which the system and strength of fiqh is established. It is a book of wondrous composition, magnificent arrangement, correct style, and beautiful structure. There is no doubt about the excellence of its composition and the beauty of its arrangement; there is no village beyond Abadan. But it is difficult to reach, stubborn in control; there is no way to attain knowledge of its subtleties and marvels, nor any path to encompass its paths and wonders, except for one who devotes himself entirely to its verification and acquisition, and tightens his resolve to encompass its entirety and detail, after being granted a clear mind for acquiring knowledge and a heart free from the whispers of false hopes, and who is deeply versed in rulings and branches, and encompasses what has been transmitted and heard in them.' End quote. Thus Allah decreed for this great book that until now it has not received its share of scholarly service befitting its high and lofty status. It has not been printed individually except in defective commercial editions, with omissions in many places, and likewise the editions that came with its old and modern commentaries. Allah has honored me and facilitated its verification, and helped me serve it, relying on ten precious manuscript copies, the oldest dated 651 AH. Praise be to Allah for His bounty and kindness. But the generous one's habit is to bestow favor on the weak and grant. And among the additional favors of my Lord is that He facilitated for me also the verification and service of the book 'Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi' by the imam, muhaddith, hafiz, faqih, usuli, versatile in many sciences, the verifier, precise, brilliant scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, d. 879 AH, based on two copies: the author's copy in his own hand, and a copy in the hand of his student, who read it to him and he authorized him with it in his handwriting. And the scholar Qasim, while engaged in his takhrij of the book's hadiths and reports and his deduction of many issues, did not neglect to record some usul corrections and evidentiary observations regarding the author despite his great imamate. Thus I combined the two books - the usul and the hadith - in one volume, and placed the takhrij of each hadith and report in its place in Usul al-Bazdawi, uniting the branch with the root, and by Allah's grace the collection was completed. My methodology in producing Usul al-Bazdawi and my primary intention was: to strive and endeavor to establish a sound text of the book from the manuscript copies while consulting the commentaries, without commentary; because explaining its obscure points and commentary would require many lines and sentences beyond the scope here, and whoever wants to pursue its demands and attain his desire: its commentaries are readily available. This, and I have endeavored to present it to the esteemed readers in a bright garment pleasing to the eye, while dividing its text and issues, adding punctuation, correcting problematic words, and prefacing it with a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi to the extent possible, along with a study of the book investigating its name, mentioning its commentaries, explaining its methodology, collecting its merits, and scholars' praise for it. I also made a comparison between it and the Usul of his contemporary Imam al-Sarakhsi, from which it became apparent to me initially that Usul al-Sarakhsi is like a commentary on it. Allah knows best. And I proceeded in this manner also in serving the book of Takhrij of its hadiths.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to his critical edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul (Kanz al-Wusul). He begins by quoting al-Bukhari al-Hanafi's praise from his commentary Kashf al-Asrar, emphasizing the book's high rank, unique style, and difficulty. The editor then laments the lack of proper scholarly edition, noting that previous prints had omissions. He explains his methodology: he used ten manuscripts, the oldest from 651 AH, to establish a sound text without adding commentary, as many commentaries already exist. He also included a companion work, Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi by Ibn Qutlubugha, reconciling the two. Additionally, he provides a biography of al-Bazdawi, a study of the book's name and commentaries, and a comparison with al-Sarakhsi's Usul. The focus is on editorial procedure, not on teaching usul al-fiqh content.

Key Terms
تخريج الأحاديث (Takhrij al-Ahadith): The process of tracing hadiths to their original sources and verifying their authenticity.
قاسم بن قُطلوبغا (Qasim ibn Qutlubugha): A Hanafi scholar and muhaddith (d. 879 AH) who wrote Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi.
نسخة المؤلف بخطه (Nuskhat al-Mu'allif bi-khattihi): The author's autograph copy, considered the most authoritative for textual criticism.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter

Editorial Methodology for Hanafi Usul Texts
Editor's preface describing his methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the methodology of a critical edition of a Hanafi usul text and identify how textual decisions impact the reliability of rulings.

Core Idea
A scholar's methodology in editing a text determines its reliability for deriving rulings.

This lesson explores the editor's preface to a critical edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul. Understanding how a text is established is crucial for any student of usul al-fiqh, because the soundness of the source text directly affects the validity of juristic reasoning. The editor describes his use of manuscripts, his reliance on commentaries, and his decision not to add extensive annotations. Let's examine what this means for the reader.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary goal
The editor states his 'primary intention' is to establish a correct text using manuscripts and commentaries without extensive annotation.
He prioritizes textual accuracy over original commentary.
2
Understand the sources used
He used two manuscripts: the author's autograph and a student's copy read to the author with ijazah. This ensures high reliability.
Using the autograph and a verified student copy increases confidence.
3
Note the treatment of subsidiary texts
He combined al-Bazdawi's Usul with Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's takhrij, placing each hadith authentication in its proper place within the usul text.
This integration makes the takhrij immediately useful.
4
Recognize the relationship with other works
The editor notes that al-Sarakhsi's Usul serves as a commentary on al-Bazdawi's, providing a valuable resource for readers seeking deeper explanation.
This insight helps navigate the Hanafi usul tradition.
5
Appreciate the humility and scope
The editor admits potential flaws and invites corrections, showing scholarly integrity. He also includes a biography and study of the book.
Humility is a hallmark of reliable scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصولي المفنّن في علوم كثيرة، المحقق المدقق البارع العلامة قاسم بن قُطلوبغا، المتوفى سنة ٨٧٩هـ، وذلك على نسختين: نسخة المؤلف بخطه، ونسخة بخط تلميذه، وقد قرأها عليه وأجازه بها بخطه. ولم ينشغل العلامةُ قاسم وهو في خِضَمَ تخريجه لأحاديث الكتاب وآثاره واستدلاله لمسائل عديدة عن تسجيل بعض الاستدراكات الأصولية، والملاحظات الاستدلالية على صاحب الكتاب مع إمامته الكبرى. وهكذا جمعت بين الكتابين الأصولي والحديثي في دفتي مجلد واحد، وأنزلتُ تخريج كل حديث وأثر في مكانه من أصول البزدوي، والتقى الفرع بالأصل، وتم ولله الحمد جَمْعُ الشمل. وكان من منهجي في إخراج كتاب أصول البزدوي وقصدي الأول: الاجتهاد والسعي لإثبات نص صحيح للكتاب من خلال النُّسَخ الخطية مع مراجعة الشروح، دون التعليق عليه ؛ لأن إيضاح مُغلَقاته وشرحها يحتاج إلى جُمَل وسطورٍ يَضيق المقام عنها، ومن أراد الوقوف على طلبته، وتحصيل بغيته : فشروحه متوافرة بكل يسر. هذا، وقد اجتهدت في تقديمه للقراء الكرام بحُلَّةٍ مُشرِقةٍ تَسرُّ الناظرين، مع القيام بتفقير نصه ومسائله، ووضع علامات الترقيم، وضَبْطِ ما أشكل من ألفاظه، وقدمت له بترجمة للإمام البزدوي بحسب الوسع والطاقة مع دراسة عن الكتاب بتحقيق اسمه وذكر شروحه، وبيان منهجه وجمع مزاياه وثناء العلماء عليه. كما عملت مقارنةً بينه وبين أصول عصريه الإمام السرخسي، والتي تبين لي من خلالها مبدئياً أن أصول السرخسي بمثابة شرح له، والله أعلم. وهكذا سِرْتُ على هذا المنوال أيضاً في خدمة كتاب تخريج أحاديثه للعلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا من التوجه لإخراج نصه الصحيح، والعناية بضمه لأصله، دون التعليق عليه كما سيأتي بيان هذا إن شاء الله. وحاشا أن أدَّعِي في عملي البراءة من العيوب، فالضَّعْفُ مما جبل عليه البشر، وحسبي أني اجتهدت، ورحم الله امرءاً أهدى إلي عيوبي». وأسأل الله من فضله العظيم السداد والصواب، والإخلاص والقبول، وأن يزيدنا من فضله، ويوفقنا ما حيينا لخدمة دينه الحنيف، مع الرضا والرضوان والعفو والعافية وأن يغفر لنا ولوالدينا ولمشايخنا وأزواجنا وأولادنا وأحبابنا ولكل من له حق علينا وللمسلمين والمسلمات، الأحياء منهم والأموات. ونسأله جل وعلا باسمه العظيم الأعظم وهو أرحم الراحمين كرماً منه وفضلاً وإحساناً أن يُعجِّل بالفَرَج عن المسلمين عامة، وعن أهل الشام خاصة، وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم تسليماً كثيراً، والحمد الله أولاً وآخراً. وكتبه سَائِد بن محمد يحيى بكداش جامعة طيبة بالمدينة المنورة قسم الدراسات الإسلامية
The versatile scholar in many sciences, the verifying, scrutinizing, brilliant scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, deceased 879 AH, based on two manuscripts: the author's copy in his handwriting, and a copy in the handwriting of his student, who read it to him and he granted him permission (ijazah) with it in his handwriting. And scholar Qasim, while engaged in his takhrij of the hadiths and reports of the book and his reasoning for numerous issues, did not neglect to record some usul corrections and evidential observations on the author despite his great imamate. Thus I combined the two books, usuli and hadithi, in the covers of one volume, and placed the takhrij of each hadith and report in its place from Usul al-Bazdawi, so the branch met the root, and by Allah's grace the gathering was completed. And it was part of my methodology in producing the book Usul al-Bazdawi and my primary intention: to strive and endeavor to establish a correct text of the book through the manuscripts while reviewing the commentaries, without annotating it, because clarifying its obscurities and explaining them would require sentences and lines that space does not permit, and whoever wishes to understand its requirements and attain his goal – its commentaries are readily available. This, and I have strived to present it to the noble readers in a bright garb that pleases the viewers, while doing tafqir (numbering) of its text and issues, placing punctuation marks, and correcting what was problematic of its expressions, and I prefaced it with a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi to the extent of capacity and ability, along with a study of the book: verifying its name, mentioning its commentaries, explaining its methodology, collecting its merits, and the praise of scholars upon it. Also, I made a comparison between it and the Usul of his contemporary Imam al-Sarakhsi, from which it became clear to me preliminarily that al-Sarakhsi's Usul is like a commentary on it, and Allah knows best. And thus I proceeded in the same manner also in serving the book of takhrij of its hadiths by scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, aiming to produce its correct text and attending to attaching it to its original, without commentary as will be explained, insha'Allah. Far be it from me to claim in my work freedom from defects, for weakness is part of human nature, and it suffices me that I strove, and may Allah have mercy on a person who points out my faults to me. And I ask Allah of His immense bounty for correctness and rightness, sincerity and acceptance, and that He increases us from His bounty, and grants us success as long as we live to serve His true religion, with pleasure and contentment, forgiveness and well-being, and that He forgives us, our parents, our teachers, our spouses, our children, our loved ones, and everyone who has a right upon us, and Muslim men and women, the living among them and the dead. And we ask Him, exalted and high, by His great and greatest name, and He is the Most Merciful of those who show mercy, out of generosity, bounty, and beneficence, to hasten relief for all Muslims, especially the people of Sham, and may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them abundant peace, and praise be to Allah first and last. Written by Sa'id ibn Muhammad Yahya Bakdash, Taibah University, Madinah al-Munawwarah, Department of Islamic Studies.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the editor's preface to the new edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul. It opens by praising the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), who wrote a takhrij (hadith authentication) of the ahadith and athar in al-Bazdawi's work. The editor explains that he combined two manuscripts: the author's autograph and a student's copy read to the author. He then describes his methodology: his primary goal was to establish a correct text of the book through manuscripts and review of commentaries, without adding his own lengthy commentary due to space constraints, and he notes that numerous commentaries are available for those seeking detailed explanation. He also included a biography of al-Bazdawi, a study of the book's name and merits, and made a comparison with al-Sarakhsi's Usul, concluding that al-Sarakhsi's work effectively serves as a commentary on al-Bazdawi's. He then mentions his similar approach to the takhrij book, and concludes with a humble disclaimer and supplications. This front matter provides the reader with the editor's scholarly credentials and methodology, establishing the authority and care behind the edition.

Key Terms
المحقق (al-muhaqqiq): The editor/critical editor who verifies and establishes a correct text
تخريج (takhrij): The process of tracing and authenticating hadiths and reports to their sources

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Al-Bazdawi's is a commentary on al-Sarakhsi's.
D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
The editor's careful methodology ensures the text's reliability, and his decision not to over-annotate keeps the focus on the original work.

Major Commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi
Listing major commentaries with details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three major commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi and state their key features and significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi's precision demanded great commentaries; three stand out: al-Kafi, Kashf al-Asrar, and al-Taqrir.

The study of Hanafi usul al-fiqh rests on foundational texts, and Usul al-Bazdawi is among the most revered. Its dense language and deep meanings prompted some of the greatest Hanafi scholars to produce commentaries. This lesson introduces three of the most significant published commentaries, their authors, and their distinguishing features, providing a roadmap for students exploring this rich tradition.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the central text
Identify Usul al-Bazdawi as a foundational Hanafi usul work. Understand why it attracted commentaries: its precise yet difficult expressions.
The author mentions the great status of the work among Hanafi scholars.
2
Identify the three commentaries in chronological order
List the three major published commentaries by author death date: al-Sighnaqi (d. 714 AH), al-Bukhari (d. 730 AH), and al-Babarti (d. 786 AH).
Order is by wafat precedence as the author states.
3
Analyze each commentary's features
For each, note the title, the author, the number of volumes, and any special remarks: al-Kafi (5 vols), Kashf al-Asrar (greatest, needs academic work), al-Taqrir (8 vols).
Al-Bukhari's commentary is described as the most beneficial.
4
Appreciate the scholarly effort
Reflect on the effort these scholars invested—al-Baghdadi's 27 years on Idah al-Maknun shows the dedication typical of such projects.
The aside about al-Baghdadi illustrates the immense labor behind Islamic scholarship.

وبخاصة أن نُسخ أصول البزدوي كثيرةٌ تبلغ المئات، فلعله اطلع في أحدها على هذا الاسم، فدونه ، ومع هذا فيبقى في الأمر نظر، والله أعلم. - وأذكر هنا بهذه المناسبة فائدةً عن البغدادي هذا صاحب الذيلين، أنه بقي في جمع إيضاح المكنون أكثر من ٢٧ سنة متواصلة، حيث بدأ بجمعه سنة ١٢٩٦هـ، وسجل هو في كتابه إيضاح المكنون ١٥٨/١ عند ذكره لكتابه : إيضاح المكنون، أنه في سنة ١٣٢٣ هـ كان لا يزال مشغولاً بإكماله، وهو في قرية: مقري كوبي»، قرب القسطنطينية.

شروح أصول البزدوي
شَرَحَ أصول البزدوي جماعةٌ من كبار الأئمة الأعلام ، وأولوه خدمةً عظيمة من التوضيح والبيان لدقة ،ألفاظه وخفاء معانيه ؛ ليُخرجوا لطلبة العلم مكنون عباراته، ويكشفوا لهم أسرار رموزه وألفاظه، ويزيدوا على شأنه نوره نوراً، وما ذاك إلا لعظيم مكانته عندهم، ونفاسته ورفعة كتب أصول الحنفية، وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفتُ عليه من ذلك، مقدماً ذكر المطبوع منها، ومرتباً لها بحسب أسبقية وفاة صاحبها:

And especially that the copies of Usul al-Bazdawi are numerous, reaching hundreds; perhaps he came across this name in one of them, so he recorded it, yet there remains doubt in the matter, and Allah knows best. - And I mention here on this occasion a benefit from al-Baghdadi, the author of the two supplements, that he spent more than 27 consecutive years compiling Idah al-Maknun, having started its compilation in 1296 AH. He recorded in his book Idah al-Maknun (1/158) when mentioning his book Idah al-Maknun that in 1323 AH he was still occupied completing it, while in the village of 'Mukri Kobi' near Constantinople.

Commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi
A group of great leading imams commented on Usul al-Bazdawi, rendering it a great service of clarification and explanation due to the precision of its expressions and the hiddenness of its meanings, to bring out for students the hidden content of its phrases, uncover for them the secrets of its symbols and words, and add light upon its light. That is only due to its great status with them, its preciousness, and the lofty rank of the Hanafi usul books. I will mention below what I have come across of that, presenting first the published ones, and arranging them according to the precedence of the death of their author:

1- The commentary of Imam Husam al-Din Husayn ibn 'Ali al-Sighnaqi al-Hanafi (d. 714 AH), titled 'al-Kafi'. He mentioned at its end that he finished writing it at the end of Jumada al-Ula 704 AH. It is printed and verified in five volumes.

2- The commentary of Imam 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn [...] (d. 730 AH), titled 'Kashf al-Asrar'. This commentary is the greatest of the commentaries, the most beneficial and clarifying, as in Kashf al-Zunun (1/112). It is printed in four large volumes with typographically compact pages. It is in severe need of academic and typographic service.

3- The commentary of Imam Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Babarti al-Hanafi (d. 786 AH), titled 'al-Taqrir'. It is printed and verified in eight volumes.
(1) See Kashf al-Zunun 1/112.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section from a work on Usul al-Bazdawi. The author first discusses the numerous copies of Usul al-Bazdawi and mentions a benefit from al-Baghdadi regarding the compilation of Idah al-Maknun. Then, he turns to the main subject: the commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi. He emphasizes the importance of the work and lists three major commentaries in chronological order by the death date of their authors. The first is 'al-Kafi' by al-Sighnaqi, a five-volume printed and verified commentary. The second is 'Kashf al-Asrar' by 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari, considered the greatest and most beneficial commentary, printed in four volumes but in need of academic attention. The third is 'al-Taqrir' by al-Babarti, printed in eight volumes. The author cites Kashf al-Zunun for the description of the second commentary.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): A foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh work by Imam al-Bazdawi, known for its precise expressions and deep meanings.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary or explanation, specifically on Usul al-Bazdawi, aiming to clarify its difficult terms and ideas.
الكافي (al-Kafi): Commentary by al-Sighnaqi on Usul al-Bazdawi, completed in 704 AH in five volumes.
كشف الأسرار (Kashf al-Asrar): Commentary by al-Bukhari on Usul al-Bazdawi, considered the greatest and most beneficial, in four volumes.
التقرير (al-Taqrir): Commentary by al-Babarti on Usul al-Bazdawi, in eight volumes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Kashf al-Zunun, which commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi is considered the greatest and most beneficial?
A) al-Kafi by al-Sighnaqi
B) Kashf al-Asrar by al-Bukhari
C) al-Taqrir by al-Babarti
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Bazdawi's major commentaries—al-Kafi, Kashf al-Asrar, and al-Taqrir—vary in volume and quality, with Kashf al-Asrar being the most esteemed.

Mapping the Commentarial Tradition on al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul
Bibliography of commentaries on al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify different types of commentaries (sharh, ta'liqa) on al-Bazdawi's Usul and assess their significance for Hanafi usul research.

Core Idea
The commentaries on al-Bazdawi's Usul are a living record of the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

This passage presents a list of commentaries and glosses that have been written on al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul. While it may seem like a mere bibliography, it provides invaluable insight into how this foundational text was studied, expanded, and transmitted across centuries and regions. By learning to read this list critically, you will understand the depth and breadth of the Hanafi usul tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Authors and Their Regions
Scan the list and note the names, dates, and geographic affiliations (e.g., al-Jarbardi al-Shafi'i from Iran, al-Kaki from Transoxiana, al-Karlani from Khwarazm). This reveals the wide dissemination of al-Bazdawi's text.
Some authors are Hanafi, others like al-Jarbardi are Shafi'i, indicating cross-madhhab interest.
2
Classify Each Entry
Determine whether each entry is a full commentary (sharh), a brief gloss (ta'liqa), or an incomplete work. The text labels some as 'sharh' and others as 'ta'liqa'. Note that some commentaries are described as 'incomplete' (e.g., al-Tahrir).
The terms are not always explicit; sometimes you must infer from the description.
3
Assess Completeness and Availability
Check which commentaries are fully extant, which are lost or unpublished, and which are only partially available. For instance, al-Shamil is described as the largest but remains unpublished, while al-Shafi was edited at the Islamic University of Medina.
Manuscript copies are often scattered in libraries; the author notes his efforts to locate volumes.
4
Reflect on the Significance for Research
Consider how this list can guide a researcher. It points to the most important commentaries to consult, highlights gaps (e.g., missing volumes of al-Shamil), and shows the value of marginal notes (ta'liqat) found in manuscript copies.
The author even suggests that marginalia from scribes can be considered commentaries.

5. Commentary of Imam Qiwam al-Din al-Kaki (d. 749 AH), titled 'Bunyat al-Wusul', with several manuscript copies mentioned by the editor of al-Kafi 1/32.
6. Commentary of Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khwarizmi al-Karlani (d. 767 AH), author of al-Kifaya commentary on al-Hidaya, titled 'al-Shafi', edited at the Islamic University of Medina, as mentioned by the editor of al-Kafi 1/32.
7. Commentary of Imam al-Ittirazi Amir Katib al-Itqani (d. 751 AH), titled 'al-Shamil', the largest book on usul al-fiqh, in ten manuscript volumes, filled with usul, fiqh, branches, and proofs. Most of it has been edited in university theses at Imam Muhammad ibn Sa'ud University in Riyadh, but not printed. I could not find its first volume despite research to quote its introduction and record the praises it bestows on Usul al-Bazdawi.
8. Commentary of Imam Abi al-Baqa Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Diya al-Makki al-Hanafi (d. 854 AH).
9. Commentary of Imam Umar ibn Abd al-Muhsin al-Arzinjani (living in 871 AH), in two volumes.
10. Among the brief glosses on it: Gloss of Imam Hamid al-Din Ali ibn Muhammad al-Darir al-Hanafi (d. 666 AH).
11. Also a gloss by Jalal al-Din Rasul Ahmad ibn al-Tabbani al-Hanafi (d. 713 AH).
12. Among the incomplete commentaries: Commentary of Imam Ala al-Din Ali ibn Muhammad, known as Musannifak (d. 775 AH), titled 'al-Tahrir'.
13. Commentary of Imam Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Fanari (834 AH), only on its preamble.
14. Commentary of Imam al-Mawla Muhammad ibn Framuz, known as Mulla Khusraw (d. 885 AH). Had it been completed, the seekers of guidance would have attained their full aim.
15. Commentary of Mahmud ibn Muhammad al-Jawnpuri al-Faruqi al-Hindi (1062 AH), mentioned by the editor of al-Kafi for al-Saghnaqi 1/31.
16. Commentary by Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Sindi, mentioned by the editor of al-Kafi, with a manuscript copy in the Egyptian National Library under no. (K 69, A 2063).
17. Among its commentaries are al-Muwaddih and al-Shafi, as in a gloss on Kashf al-Zunun 1/113.
18. Also, we can count among its commentaries and glosses: what scribes and owners of manuscripts of Usul al-Bazdawi wrote in their margins and between lines. I have some samples that I relied on in editing the text; from these copies one can obtain many marginal notes, benefits, and glosses not found elsewhere.
For example, what appears at the end of a copy dated 800 AH: 'Praise be to God for completion, and the best prayers and peace upon His Messenger Muhammad. Written, read, corrected, and glossed by the poor and humble servant in need of the mercy of his Lord and Master: Khalil al-Rumi al-Bafi in the year eight hundred. Praise be to God who granted me its completion.'
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography from a modern edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul, listing seventeen named commentaries and glosses along with a general category of marginal notes. The author begins with commentary number 4 (the first three are presumably from earlier pages) and proceeds to describe each work's author, title, and sometimes its physical extent or current location. The list highlights the richness of the Hanafi usul tradition, with commentaries ranging from the 7th to the 11th century AH, written by scholars from diverse regions including Iran, Anatolia, Egypt, and India. Notably, some commentaries like 'al-Shamil' by al-Itqani are described as enormous (ten volumes) but remain unpublished. The author also includes incomplete works, such as al-Fanari's commentary which only covers the preamble, and expresses regret that Mulla Khusraw's commentary was never finished. The final entry notes that any marginalia found in manuscripts can be considered a form of commentary, and gives an example of a colophon by a scribe named Khalil al-Rumi. This passage serves as a valuable resource for researchers studying the reception history of al-Bazdawi's text.

Key Terms
شرح (sharḥ): A full commentary that explains the text of al-Bazdawi's Usul.
تعليقة (ta‘līqa): A short gloss or annotation on the text, often critical or supplementary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which commentary is described as 'the largest book on usul al-fiqh'?
A) al-Shafi by al-Karlani
B) al-Shamil by al-Itqani
C) al-Tahrir by Musannifak
D) Bunyat al-Wusul by al-Kaki

Key Takeaway
The commentarial tradition on al-Bazdawi's Usul is extensive and diverse; knowing it is essential for deep understanding of Hanafi usul.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Significance and Methodology of Usul al-Bazdawi
Praise and methodological description of Usul al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of Usul al-Bazdawi as described by its author and explain why it is highly regarded in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi explains texts by their meanings and defines principles by their branches, combining depth with brevity.

This passage opens a discussion of the fame and esteem of Usul al-Bazdawi, one of the foundational works in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It first highlights the widespread recognition of the book's value despite its difficulty, then quotes the author's own concise description of his methodology. Finally, it presents a glowing tribute from a later commentator, Imam al-Bukhari, which underscores the work's unique craftsmanship and lasting influence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its reputation
Read the opening lines noting how the book is described as famous and praised by scholars far and wide. Observe that even though the text is difficult, its value is acknowledged.
The passage uses phrases like 'طار صيته' (its fame flew) to emphasize widespread recognition.
2
Extract the author's stated methodology
Focus on the sentence from the author's introduction: 'هذا الكتاب لبيان النصوص بمعانيها، وتعريف الأصول بفروعها، على شرط الإيجاز والاختصار'. Understand that he aims to (a) explain nusus (texts) according to their meanings, (b) define usul (principles) through their furu' (branches), and (c) do so with brevity.
The phrase 'على شرط الإيجاز والاختصار' indicates conciseness is a deliberate constraint.
3
Analyze al-Bukhari's praise
Read Imam al-Bukhari's description from 'Kashf al-Asrar'. Note the specific qualities he highlights: 'عجيب الصنعة، رائع الترتيب، صحيح الأسلوب مليح التركيب' (amazing craftsmanship, splendid arrangement, correct style, beautiful composition). This explains the esteem despite difficulty.
Al-Bukhari was a major Hanafi commentator; his praise carries weight in the tradition.
4
Connect methodology to the book's value
Reflect on how the author's concise linking of usul and furu' likely contributed to the book's dense yet powerful nature. The difficulty in understanding (noted in the passage) stems from this very conciseness.
This relationship between brevity and depth is a recurring theme in Hanafi usul works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثناء العلماء على أصول البزدوي ووصفهم لحاله وبيانهم لمنهج مؤلفه ، إن أصول فخر الإسلام البزدوي مما اشتهر بين الأنام، وطار صيته على جميع الأيام، وشاع ذكره بين القاصي والداني من الأئمة الأعلام وعَرَفوا جلالة قدره، وعظيم مكانته، ورفعة شأنه، وقد شَرَحَه كبار الأئمة المحققين، وقرروا جميعاً قوة هذا الكتاب وأهميته البالغة، وعُلُو منزلته، ودقيق ألفاظه وعباراته ، وصعوبة فهمه، وأثنوا عليه ثناء بالغاً. و- قبل نقل كلامهم أذكر هنا لُب مقدمة المؤلف لكتابه، ففيها بيان باختصار لعمله الذي قام به ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، فقد قال رحمه الله : وهذا الكتاب لبيان النصوص بمعانيها، وتعريف الأصول بفروعها، على شرط الإيجاز والاختصار إن شاء الله تعالى وما توفيقي إلا بالله». اهـ ٢- ومن ثناء العلماء على أصول البزدوي : ما قاله الإمام علاء الدين عبد العزيز البخاري في مقدمة شرحه لأصول البزدوي «كشف الأسرار : امتاز أصولُ البزدوي من بين الكتب المصنفة في هذا الفنّ شَرَفاً وسُمُوا، وحلَّ محله مقام الثريا مجداً وعلواً، ضمن فيه أصول الشرع وأحكامه، وأدرج فيه ما به نظامُ الفقه وقوامه وهو كتاب عجيب الصنعة، رائع الترتيب، صحيح الأسلوب مليح التركيب، ليس في جودة تركيبه
Praise of the scholars for Usul al-Bazdawi and their description of its state and explanation of its author's methodology. Indeed, the Usul of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi became famous among people, its reputation flew over all days, its mention spread among near and far from the prominent imams, and they recognized the majesty of its rank, the greatness of its status, and the elevation of its standing. Senior verifying imams have commented on it, and they all affirmed the strength of this book, its extreme importance, its high station, the precision of its expressions and phrases, and the difficulty of understanding it, and they praised it extensively. Before quoting their words, I mention here the essence of the author's introduction to his book, which contains a brief explanation of his work and methodology. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'This book is for explaining the texts according to their meanings, and defining the principles by their branches, on the condition of brevity and conciseness, Allah willing. My success is only from Allah.' End. 2- Among the praise of scholars for Usul al-Bazdawi is what Imam Alauddin Abdul Aziz al-Bukhari said in the introduction of his commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi 'Kashf al-Asrar': 'Usul al-Bazdawi distinguished itself among the books written in this art in honor and loftiness, and assumed the position of the Pleiades in glory and highness. It included the principles of Shariah and its rulings, and incorporated what constitutes the system and foundation of fiqh. It is a book of amazing craftsmanship, splendid arrangement, correct style, and beautiful composition. There is none like it in the quality of its composition...'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a section titled 'Praise of Scholars for Usul al-Bazdawi'. It first describes the widespread fame and high esteem of the book among scholars. Then it quotes the author's own concise description of his work: he aimed to explain the texts (nusus) according to their meanings and to define the principles (usul) through their branches (furu'), adhering to brevity. This shows his methodology of linking principles to their applications concisely. Finally, it quotes Imam Alauddin al-Bukhari's eloquent praise from his commentary 'Kashf al-Asrar', highlighting the book's unique merit, comprehensive coverage, and excellent composition. The passage establishes the authority and importance of the work within the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
أصول (usul): Principles or foundations of Islamic jurisprudence; here referring to the science of usul al-fiqh.
فروع (furu'): Branches or derived legal rulings; the applied fiqh rules.
نصوص (nusus): Texts of revelation (Quran and Sunnah) that serve as evidence.
إيجاز (ijaz): Conciseness or brevity in expression while retaining full meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Imam al-Bukhari say about Usul al-Bazdawi's composition?
A) It is lengthy and repetitive
B) It is beautiful and well-arranged
C) It is easy and simple
D) It is outdated and obsolete

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Bazdawi is esteemed for its method of linking principles to applications concisely, blending depth with elegance.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Authority and Methodology of Usul al-Bazdawi
Praise and methodological description of Usul al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and significance of Usul al-Bazdawi and explain its methodology based on the author's own words and the commentators' praises.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi is the most challenging yet authoritative Hanafi usul text, requiring complete devotion to master.

This passage introduces one of the foundational works in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Usul al-Bazdawi. The author, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, states his methodology—to explain scriptural texts through their meanings and to define principles by linking them to their branches, all with brevity. Two major commentators, al-Bukhari and al-Babarti, praise the book's depth but emphasize its extreme difficulty, warning that only those who dedicate themselves entirely can grasp it. This sets the stage for the rigorous study ahead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
In his introduction, al-Bazdawi says what this book is for. Note the key phrase: 'بيان النصوص بمعانيها، وتعريف الأصول بفروعها'.
The book aims to explain texts by their meanings and define principles through their branches.
2
Recognize the book's reputation
From the commentators' praises, note the attributes mentioned: honor (شرف), greatness (عظمة), precision (دقة), and difficulty (صعوبة).
Al-Bukhari calls it 'amazing in construction' and 'correct in style'.
3
Understand the challenge
Both commentators explicitly state the book is difficult. Al-Bukhari says 'difficult of access, hard to master'; al-Babarti says it 'refused its goal to the students'.
This difficulty is not a flaw but a sign of depth.
4
Connect to the learning approach
Al-Bukhari says mastery is only for those who 'devote themselves entirely' (أقبل بكليته). This sets the expectation for the reader.
