ثناء العلماء على أصول البزدوي ووصفهم لحاله وبيانهم لمنهج مؤلفه ، إن أصول فخر الإسلام البزدوي مما اشتهر بين الأنام، وطار صيته على جميع الأيام، وشاع ذكره بين القاصي والداني من الأئمة الأعلام وعَرَفوا جلالة قدره، وعظيم مكانته، ورفعة شأنه، وقد شَرَحَه كبار الأئمة المحققين، وقرروا جميعاً قوة هذا الكتاب وأهميته البالغة، وعُلُو منزلته، ودقيق ألفاظه وعباراته ، وصعوبة فهمه، وأثنوا عليه ثناء بالغاً. وقبل نقل كلامهم أذكر هنا لُب مقدمة المؤلف لكتابه، ففيها بيان باختصار لعمله الذي قام به ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، فقد قال رحمه الله : وهذ الكتاب لبيان النصوص بمعانيها، وتعريف الأصول بفروعها، على شرط الإيجاز والاختصار إن شاء الله تعالى وما توفيقي إلا بالله». اهـ ومن ثناء العلماء على أصول البزدوي : ما قاله الإمام علاء الدين عبد العزيز البخاري في مقدمة شرحه لأصول البزدوي «كشف الأسرار : امتاز أصولُ البزدوي من بين الكتب المصنفة في هذا الفنّ شَرَفاً وسُمُوا، وحلَّ محله مقام الثريا مجداً وعلواً، ضمن فيه أصول الشرع وأحكامه، وأدرج فيه ما به نظامُ الفقه وقوامه وهو كتاب عجيب الصنعة، رائع الترتيب، صحيح الأسلوب مليح التركيب، ليس في جودة تركيبه وحُسن ترتيبه مريةٌ، وليس وراء عبادان قرية، لكنه صعب المرام، أبي الزمام، لا سبيل إلى الوصول إلى معرفة لطفه وغرائبه، ولا طريق إلى الإحاطة بطرقه وعجائبه إلا لمن أقبل بكليته على تحقيقه وتحصيله، وشد حيازيمه بالإحاطة بجملته وتفصيله بعد أن رزق في اقتباس العلم جلياً، وذَرْعاً من هَواجس أضاليل المُنى خليّا) ، وقد تبحر مع ذلك في الأحكام والفروع، وأحاط بما جاء فيها من المنقول والمسموع. وقد سألني إخواني في الدين وأعواني على طلب اليقين أن أكتب لهم شرحاً يكشفُ عن أوجه غوامض معانيه نقابها، ويرفع عن اللطائف المستترة في مبانيه حجابها، ويوضحُ ما أبهم من رموزه وإشاراته المعضلة، ويبين ما أجمل من ألفاظه وعباراته المشلة س وقد تحيَّرت العقولُ في حَلَ مشكلاته بعد تهالكهم في بحثه وتنقيره، وعجزت وعجزت النحاحير عن درك معضلاته، مع حرصهم على تحقيقه وتفكيره». اهـ وقال عنه الإمام البابرتي في أول شرحه «التقرير» ٧٥/١: «كتابٌ تأبَّى على الطلبة المستمدين مَرَامُه واستعصى على العلماء المحققين زمامه، يعطس بأنف شامخ من الإباء، وينبو بعطف جامع مع
Praises of the scholars on Usul al-Bazdawi, and their description of its condition and explanation of the methodology of its author. Indeed, the Usul of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi is among what became famous among people, its reputation flew over all days, and its mention spread among near and far of the eminent imams, and they recognized the majesty of its worth, the greatness of its status, and the highness of its standing. Senior verifying imams have commented on it, and all affirmed the strength of this book, its extreme importance, its lofty status, the precision of its words and expressions, and the difficulty of understanding it, and they praised it abundantly. Before quoting their words, I will mention here the core of the author's introduction to his book, for in it is a brief explanation of his work and the methodology he followed. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'This book is for explaining the texts with their meanings, and defining the principles with their branches, on the condition of brevity and conciseness, if Allah wills. And my success is only from Allah.' End quote. And from the praises of scholars on Usul al-Bazdawi: what Imam 'Ala' al-Din 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari said in the introduction to his commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi, 'Kashf al-Asrar': 'Usul al-Bazdawi stood out among the books authored in this art in honor and loftiness, and occupied the place of the Pleiades in glory and highness. It comprises the principles of the Shari'ah and its rulings, and includes what is the system of fiqh and its support. It is a book amazing in construction, splendid in arrangement, correct in style, beautiful in composition; there is no doubt about the quality of its composition and the beauty of its arrangement, and beyond 'Abbadan there is no village. But it is difficult of access, hard to master; there is no way to reach knowledge of its subtlety and rarities, nor any path to encompass its methods and wonders, except for one who devotes himself entirely to its verification and acquisition, and tightens his belt to encompass its entirety and detail, after being granted, in acquiring knowledge, a broad chest and a disposition empty from vain desires and false hopes.' And he was, moreover, deeply versed in rulings and branches, and encompassed what has come regarding them from transmitted and heard reports. And my brothers in religion and my assistants in seeking certainty asked me to write a commentary for them that would unveil the faces of its hidden meanings, remove the veils from the subtle points concealed in its structures, clarify what is ambiguous from its difficult symbols and indications, and explain what is summarized from its problematic words and expressions. Indeed, minds have been perplexed in solving its problems after their exhaustion in researching and examining it, and the acute ones have failed to grasp its difficulties, despite their eagerness to verify and contemplate it.' End quote. And Imam al-Babarti said about it in the beginning of his commentary 'al-Taqrir' (1/75): 'A book that refused its goal to the students seeking benefit, and its reins were unattainable by the verifying scholars. It blows its nose with a high nose of pride, and recoils with a comprehensive bend...'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage introduces the work 'Usul al-Bazdawi' by presenting the author's own summary of his methodology and then quoting two major Hanafi commentators—'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari (author of Kashf al-Asrar) and al-Babarti (author of al-Taqrir)—who praise the book's depth and difficulty. The passage functions as front matter, establishing the authority and challenging nature of the text. The author states that his goal is to explain scriptural texts through their meanings and to define the principles (usul) by linking them to their branches (furu'), while maintaining brevity. Al-Bukhari emphasizes the book's superior composition and arrangement but notes its extreme difficulty, accessible only to those who devote themselves entirely to its study. Al-Babarti echoes this, describing the book as resistant even to skilled scholars. This sets the stage for the reader: the work is authoritative but demands rigorous effort.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The famous Hanafi usul work by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, known for its precision and difficulty.
كشف الأسرار (Kashf al-Asrar): A commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi by Imam 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari.
التقرير (al-Taqrir): A commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi by Imam al-Babarti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Purpose of al-Taqrir: Commenting on al-Bazdawi's Usul
Commentator's preface justifying his commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the title and author of the commentary al-Taqrir and explain why the commentator wrote it.

Core Idea
Al-Taqrir is a later commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul, written to clarify its difficulties.

This passage is the commentator's preface to his explanation of al-Bazdawi's foundational text on Hanafi usul al-fiqh. He praises the original work's depth and difficulty, then announces his commentary 'al-Taqrir li-Usul Fakhr al-Islam'. Understanding this preface helps situate the commentary within the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Determine which book is being commented upon. The preface refers to 'Usul Fakhr al-Islam' meaning al-Bazdawi's usul work.
Al-Bazdawi is also known as Fakhr al-Islam.
2
Note the commentator's motivation
The commentator states that colleagues requested a clear explanation because the original text is difficult. He aims to unveil its obscurities.
The commentary is named al-Taqrir ('the establishment').
3
Recognize scholarly endorsements
Quotes from al-Babarti and Ibn Khaldun are given to emphasize the stature of al-Bazdawi's work and the need for a commentary.
Both scholars attest to the book's profundity.

وحُسن ترتيبه مريةٌ، وليس وراء عبادان قرية، لكنه صعب المرام، أبي الزمام، لا سبيل إلى الوصول إلى معرفة لطفه وغرائبه، ولا طريق إلى الإحاطة بطرقه وعجائبه إلا لمن أقبل بكليته على تحقيقه وتحصيله، وشد حيازيمه بالإحاطة بجملته وتفصيله بعد أن رزق في اقتباس العلم جلياً، وذَرْعاً من هَواجس أضاليل المُنى خليّا) ، وقد تبحر مع ذلك في الأحكام والفروع، وأحاط بما جاء فيها من المنقول والمسموع. وقد سألني إخواني في الدين وأعواني على طلب اليقين أن أكتب لهم شرحاً يكشفُ عن أوجه غوامض معانيه نقابها، ويرفع عن اللطائف المستترة في مبانيه حجابها، ويوضحُ ما أبهم من رموزه وإشاراته المعضلة، ويبين ما أجمل من ألفاظه وعباراته المشكلة.
وقد تحيَّرت العقولُ في حَلَ مشكلاته بعد تهالكهم في بحثه وتنقيره، وعجزت النحاحير عن درك معضلاته، مع حرصهم على تحقيقه وتفكيره.

فانظر كيف أخبر هذان الحبران - يعني شيخه وشيخ شيخه- عن نبوة الطلبة من هذا الكتاب، وكبوة الطلبة في حَلْبته. فشرعتُ عاملاً لله، متوكلاً على الله، مستعيناً بالله في تحرير ما أحاوله، وتقرير ما أقاوله من تأليف شرح مختصر لا يُخل إيجازه، ويحصل في أيسر مدةٍ إنجازه، يُظهِر خفاياه، ويُخبر عن خباياه، يُبين ضمائره، ويعين سرائره، وتصديتُ لتقييد أوابده، وإطلاق شواهده، ونشر فوائده، ونَظْم قلائده، ... وسميته : «التقرير لأصول فخر الإسلام»، وسألت الله أن ينفع به كما نفع بأصله طلبة الإسلام.

It sneezes with a lofty nose of pride and recoils with a comprehensive bend along with refractoriness. Its words have become closed, its symbols and indications hidden. It contains from the principles secrets that none but Allah can unveil, and it blazes in the branches with lights of moons that have no eclipses in the Sharia of Allah.' So see how these two scholars - meaning his teacher and his teacher's teacher - informed of the students' inability regarding this book and their stumbling in its arena. So I set out, working for Allah, relying on Allah, seeking help from Allah in writing what I intend and composing what I discuss from a concise commentary whose abridgment does not diminish, and whose completion is achieved in the shortest time. It reveals its hidden aspects, informs about its secrets, clarifies its implications, and specifies its inner meanings. I undertook to record its loose ends, release its testimonies, spread its benefits, and string its necklaces. And I named it 'al-Taqrir li-Usul Fakhr al-Islam'. And I asked Allah to benefit by it just as He benefited by its original the students of Islam. And the distinguished judge Ibn Khaldun (d. 808 AH) said in his Muqaddimah: 'As for the Usul of the Hanafis, they have written much in it... and the best writing of the later scholars in it is the composition of Sayf al-Islam al-Bazdawi, one of their imams, and it is comprehensive.' I said: thus it is Sayf al-Islam, and his fame is as Fakhr al-Islam. And the great professor Dr. Ibrahim Shabuh, may Allah preserve him, informed me gratefully in a telephone conversation with him in Tunis that the four manuscript copies he relied on in editing Ibn Khaldun read thus: Sayf al-Islam. And in the biography of the distinguished scholar Sheikh Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Shaw'an (d. 822 AH), a student of al-Haddad, author of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, it is mentioned that he used to say...

Commentary
This passage is the commentary author's introduction to his explanation of al-Bazdawi's Usul. He begins by praising the original book, acknowledging its difficulty and the intense effort required to master it. He then mentions that his peers requested a clear commentary, and he responds by writing a concise work named 'al-Taqrir li-Usul Fakhr al-Islam'. He quotes al-Babarti's praise of the original text, highlighting its profundity, and Ibn Khaldun's recognition of al-Bazdawi as the best later writer on Hanafi usul. The commentary aims to clarify ambiguities, explain symbols, and make the text accessible without sacrificing depth.

Key Terms
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Honorific title for al-Bazdawi, meaning 'Pride of Islam'.
التقرير (al-Taqrir): Title of the commentary being introduced; means 'the establishment' or 'the confirmation'.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Understanding the Merits of Usul al-Bazdawi
Describing features and importance of Usul al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three key features of Usul al-Bazdawi that distinguish it as a foundational Hanafi usul text and explain how it integrates evidence from multiple sources.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi grounds Hanafi usul in diverse proofs and bridges theory with practice.

This passage introduces the merits of Imam al-Bazdawi's usul work, a cornerstone of the Hanafi scholarly tradition. It highlights how al-Bazdawi systematically proves usul principles using Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational argument, and then applies them to numerous fiqh branches. As a student of Hanafi usul, understanding these features helps you appreciate the rigor and comprehensiveness of the method you are learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources of evidence used
In the passage, find the list of sources al-Bazdawi uses to support usul principles: the Book (Quran), Sunnah, Ijma (consensus), and al-ma'qul (rational proofs). Note that he also includes linguistic evidence from Arabic poetry and rhetoric.
These correspond to the classical Hanafi hierarchy of evidence.
2
Recognize the treatment of ikhtilaf
The passage states that al-Bazdawi records disagreements within the Hanafi school and between Hanafis and others (especially Shafi'is). This shows his awareness of different views and his effort to provide rigorous discussions.
This feature makes the book a valuable record of historical usul debates.
3
Observe the connection between usul and furu
After each usul principle, al-Bazdawi provides many branches (furu') and applications. This demonstrates how theoretical principles yield concrete fiqh rulings.
The author remarks that examples are too many to count, emphasizing the practical orientation.
4
Note the authorial style
Al-Bazdawi rarely cites sources explicitly, except for Zahir al-Riwaya and al-Muntaqa. He also updates his own views when needed, showing intellectual honesty.
This reflects a mature ijtihad methodology.

مزايا وخصائص أصول البزدوي

ثم إنه بعد ذلك يذكر عقيب كل قاعدة في الاستنباط فروعاً كثيرة، وشواهد وتطبيقات عديدة، يبين فيها بناء الفروع على الأصول، وكثيراً ما يختمها بقوله : والأمثلة على ذلك أكثر من أن تُحصى».

Page 33: 'Whoever knows al-Kashshaf by al-Zamakhshari and the great Usul al-Bazdawi knows all the sciences. He, may Allah have mercy on him, had complete knowledge of both, often studied them, and solved their difficulties. At first, some issues in al-Bazdawi were problematic for him, but after a while they became clear to him with evident clarity.' End quote from what was problematic to him from all. * And about him the author of Kashf al-Zunun (d. 1067 AH) said (1/112): 'It is a book of great importance, magnificent in proof, containing subtle considerations in the briefest expressions, its meaning refuses and its reins are difficult for scholars, its expressions are intricate and its symbols and allusions hidden, so a group of outstanding scholars undertook the burden of its elucidation and uncovering its hidden aspects and hints.' * And Imam al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) said in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 124: 'Usul al-Bazdawi is a great book ... reliable and authoritative.' As for the sources of al-Bazdawi in his usul, the author mostly creates the text of his words and expressions without attributing to previous books except rarely. He explicitly cites from the books of Zahir al-Riwaya by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and al-Muntaqa by al-Hakim al-Shahid. He also quotes his teachers without mentioning their names or the names of their books. He transmitted the views of Imam 'Isa ibn Aban, al-Karkhi, and al-Jassas, and followed the statements of Imam al-Shafi'i, quoting and discussing them, all without naming any book of these imams from whom he quoted. 4. From the methodology of Imam al-Bazdawi: he used to announce the change of his views and ijtihad if that occurred, such as the issue of the obligation of rulings on a minor, p. 0713. ***** Page 34: Merits and Characteristics of Usul al-Bazdawi. 1. One of the greatest characteristics and merits of Usul al-Bazdawi is that Imam al-Bazdawi in it provided evidence for the usuli principles upon which the Hanafi school is based, upon which the derivation of rulings from specific evidences is built. This is a very important matter, namely knowing the foundations of these principles and their bases built upon various evidences. He brought proofs from the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and reason, mentioning the aspect of indication from the texts. He also mentions many evidences from the Arabic language, Arabic poetry, and the sciences of meanings and rhetoric for issues related to derivation and judgment through linguistic interpretation of words, such as the wording of oaths, acknowledgments, divorce, and the like, especially in the chapter on particles of meanings. 2. Another distinction of Usul al-Bazdawi is that it mentions the disagreements occurring in the principles of derivation within the Hanafi school among its imams and prominent scholars, as well as the disagreement between Hanafis and others, especially the Shafi'is, mentioning precise discussions of the proofs of other views and the back-and-forth among them. Then, after that, he mentions following each principle in derivation many branches, numerous evidences and applications, showing the building of branches upon principles, often ending with: 'And examples of that are more than can be counted.' Thus this book is truly comprehensive of both principles and branches. Among its merits is that it quotes from the books of the imams of the school to authenticate what he records.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an introduction extolling the virtues of al-Bazdawi's work on usul al-fiqh, which is foundational for the Hanafi school. It begins with a quote from an unnamed scholar who claims that mastery of al-Zamakhshari's tafsir and al-Bazdawi's usul constitutes knowledge of all sciences—an indication of the book's comprehensive nature. The writer then cites authorities like Kashf al-Zunun and Imam al-Laknawi to affirm the book's stature and difficulty. A key methodological note is that al-Bazdawi rarely cites his sources explicitly, except for works of Zahir al-Riwaya and al-Muntaqa; he often transmits views from earlier Hanafi masters like 'Isa ibn Aban, al-Karkhi, and al-Jassas, as well as from Imam al-Shafi'i, without naming specific books. This reflects the author's independent style and deep engagement with the tradition. The passage then lists three main merits: (1) al-Bazdawi grounds Hanafi usul principles in detailed evidence from Quran, Sunnah, ijma, and reason, including linguistic analysis from Arabic poetry and rhetoric; (2) he records internal Hanafi disagreements as well as debates with other schools (especially Shafi'is), providing rigorous argumentation; (3) he follows each principle with numerous practical branches (furu') and applications, showing how theory produces fiqh rulings, often ending with the remark that examples are too many to count. The work thus bridges usul and furu'. Finally, the author notes al-Bazdawi's practice of changing his own views when evidence warrants, citing an example regarding obligations on minors.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh work by Imam al-Bazdawi, characterized by comprehensive proofs, inter-school debates, and application of principles to branches.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwaya): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that represent the authoritative transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
المنتقى (al-Muntaqa): A collection of hadith and fiqh rulings by al-Hakim al-Shahid, used as a source by al-Bazdawi.
المعقول (al-ma'qul): Rational proofs or reasoning, used alongside scriptural sources (Quran, Sunnah, ijma) to establish usul principles.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Mazaya wa Khasa'is Usul al-Bazdawi: Features and Merits
Describing the features and merits of al-Bazdawi's work on usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of Usul al-Bazdawi and explain how its methodology supports the Hanafi school's usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi masterfully integrates proofs, intra-school disagreements, and practical applications to solidify Hanafi usul.

This lesson introduces the celebrated work 'Usul al-Bazdawi' by Imam al-Bazdawi, a cornerstone of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Imam al-Bazdawi systematically proves the Hanafi school's principles using a wide range of evidence, from Quran and Sunnah to linguistic analysis and rational argument. He also documents internal and cross-madhhab debates, linking each theoretical principle to concrete legal branches. Understanding these features will help you appreciate why this text is revered and how its deliberate difficulty preserves the integrity of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six distinct features
Carefully read the passage and list the six features or merits explicitly mentioned. They include: (1) proving Hanafi rules with diverse proofs, (2) recording internal and external differences, (3) linking principles to branches, (4) relying on authoritative sources, (5) refuting the Mu'tazila, and (6) the deliberate difficulty of the text.
The features are enumerated with numbers in the original text.
2
Explain the significance of each feature
For each feature, ask: Why does al-Bazdawi emphasise this? For example, linguistic analysis is crucial for interpreting texts correctly, and including furu' shows how usul operates in practice.
3
Relate the features to al-Bazdawi's methodology
Consider how these features together create a comprehensive methodology: evidence-based, inclusive of differing views, applied, authoritatively sourced, polemical, and gate-keeping.
4
Evaluate the purpose of the text's difficulty
The passage states that difficulty is a merit, not a flaw. Discuss why al-Bazdawi would intentionally make his work challenging, and how this protects the field of ijtihad.
Refer to the common misunderstanding about difficulty being a flaw.

مزايا وخصائص أصول البزدوي
١ - إن من أعظم خصائص أصول البزدوي ومزاياه أن الإمام البزدوي دلل فيه على ما قام عليه مذهب الحنفية من القواعد الأصولية التي تم عليها بناء استنباط الأحكام من الأدلة التفصيلية، وهذا أمر مهم جداً، وهو معرفة مباني هذه القواعد وأسسها التي بنيت عليها من مختلف الأدلة. فقد أتى على ذلك بأدلة من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والمعقول مع ذكر وجه الدلالة من النصوص، كما يذكر شواهد كثيرة من اللغة العربية والشعر العربي، وعلم المعاني والبديع للمسائل التي يتعلق بها الاستنباط والحكم بتفسير اللفظ لغوياً، كألفاظ الأيمان والإقرارات والطلاق ونحو ذلك، ولا سيما في باب حروف المعاني. ۲- ومما يمتاز به أصول البزدوي أنه يذكر الخلاف الواقع في قواعد الاستنباط ضمن المذهب الحنفي بين أئمته وأعلامه، وكذلك الخلاف بين الحنفية وغيرهم وبخاصة الشافعية مع ذكر المناقشات الدقيقة لأدلة الأقوال الأخرى والأخذ والرد بينها.
ثم إنه بعد ذلك يذكر عقيب كل قاعدة في الاستنباط فروعاً كثيرة، وشواهد وتطبيقات عديدة، يبين فيها بناء الفروع على الأصول، وكثيراً ما يختمها بقوله : والأمثلة على ذلك أكثر من أن تُحصى».
وبهذا يكون هذا الكتاب جامعاً في الحقيقة بين الأصول والفروع.
ومن مزاياه أنه ينقل عن كتب أئمة المذهب لتوثيق ما يدونه ويذهب إليه كالإمام محمد بن الحسن في كتبه ظاهر الرواية والنوادر، وينقل عن الإمام الحاكم الشهيد في المنتقى، وكذلك عن الإمام الكرخي والجصاص، وغيرهم، كما ينقل كثيراً عن مشايخه دون أن يسميهم، فيقول : قال بعض مشايخنا.
يهتم بالرد على المعتزلة وأصولهم التي بنوا عليها مذهبهم.
٦ - وبعد هذا كله وقبلَه : فهو كتاب عمدة عند السادة الحنفية، معتبر عند المتقدمين والمتأخرين من أئمة علماء أصول الفقه.
يمتاز هذا الكتاب بأنه كتاب تراثي قديم عال، مبارك رفيع، لأستاذ أئمة السلف، ولإمام كبير من أئمة الدنيا في الفروع والأصول، وعليه فالعيش مع هؤلاء الكبار العظام يُنتج كباراً، ودراسة مثل هذه المصنفات العالية، والدخول في أنوارها وبركاتها تولد همةً ونشاطاً، وتُورث بركةً وخيراً كبيراً.
إذا ما علا المرء رام العُلا ويقنع بالدُّونَ مَن كان دُونا
ولعل من مزايا هذا الكتاب صعوبة فهمه وتعسّر إدراك محتواه، وذلك حتى لا يستطيع الإقبال على علم قواعد استنباط الأحكام إلا من كان أهلاً لذلك، وحتى يخرج بذلك الأدعياء، ويعرف كل حده ليقف عنده، فالأمر ليس بهذه السهولة التي يُصوِّرها البعض للقيام بالاجتهاد والترجيح بين أقوال كبار الأئمة، فضلاً عن العمل، والتي جرأت الكثير للدخول في ذلك وهم لا يفقهون حديثاً، والله المستعان.
Features and Characteristics of Usul al-Bazdawi: 1. Among the greatest features and merits of Usul al-Bazdawi is that Imam al-Bazdawi proved therein the usuli principles upon which the Hanafi school is based, principles upon which the derivation of rulings from detailed evidences is built. This is a very important matter, which is knowing the foundations and bases of these principles built upon various evidences. He brought proofs from the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and reason, mentioning the implication of the texts, and he also mentioned many witnesses from the Arabic language, Arabic poetry, and the sciences of meaning and rhetoric for issues related to derivation and ruling by linguistic interpretation of words, such as the words of oaths, acknowledgments, divorce, and the like, especially concerning particles of meaning. 2. Another distinguishing feature of Usul al-Bazdawi is that it mentions the differences occurring in the principles of derivation within the Hanafi school among its imams and prominent figures, as well as the differences between Hanafis and others, especially the Shafi'is, with precise discussions of the proofs of other views and the back-and-forth between them. Then, after each principle of derivation, he mentions many branches, witnesses, and numerous applications, showing the construction of branches on principles, often concluding with: 'The examples of that are too many to count.' Thus this book is truly comprehensive of both principles and branches. Among its merits is that he transmits from the books of the imams of the school to authenticate what he records and adopts, such as Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in his books of Zahir al-Riwaya and al-Nawadir, and he transmits from Imam al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Muntaqa, and also from Imam al-Karkhi and al-Jassas, and others. He also frequently transmits from his teachers without naming them, saying: 'One of our teachers said.' He is concerned with refuting the Mu'tazila and their principles upon which they built their school. 6. After all this and before it, it is a foundational book for the Hanafis, esteemed by early and later imams of usul al-fiqh scholars. This book is distinguished as an ancient, high, blessed, lofty heritage book, written by a master of the imams of the predecessors, a great imam among the imams of the world in branches and principles. Therefore, living with these great and grand figures produces great ones, and studying such high compositions and entering into their lights and blessings generates ambition and activity, and bequeaths great blessing and goodness. If a person rises high, he seeks highness, but one who is low is content with lowliness. Perhaps among the merits of this book is its difficulty of understanding and the challenge of grasping its content, so that only those who are worthy can approach the science of the principles of deriving rulings, and so that pretenders are excluded, and everyone knows their limit and stops there. The matter is not as easy as some depict to perform ijtihad and weighing between the statements of the great imams, let alone practice, which has emboldened many to enter into that while they do not understand even a hadith. Allah is the Helper.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage serves as an introduction to the book 'Usul al-Bazdawi', outlining its distinctive features and the methodology of its author, Imam al-Bazdawi. The text first highlights that al-Bazdawi provides proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational evidence to support the Hanafi principles of usul al-fiqh. He also demonstrates the implication (wajh al-dalala) from these texts. Additionally, he draws on linguistic evidence from Arabic, poetry, and rhetoric, particularly in interpreting particles of meaning. Second, the book records internal disagreements within the Hanafi school on matters of usul, as well as debates with other schools, especially the Shafi'is. Third, after each usul principle, al-Bazdawi gives numerous furu' (branches) and applications to show how principles translate into actual rulings. Fourth, the author relies on authoritative Hanafi sources like Imam Muhammad's Zahir al-Riwaya and Nawadir, as well as works of al-Hakim al-Shahid, al-Karkhi, and al-Jassas. He also references his own teachers without naming them. Fifth, the book refutes the Mu'tazila. Sixth, it is established as a foundational text for Hanafis. Finally, the passage notes the deliberate difficulty of the book, which ensures that only those qualified to engage in ijtihad can grasp it, preventing pretenders from claiming such authority. This commentary underscores the book's role as a comprehensive and authoritative source in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the most authoritative sources of the Hanafi school.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): The rare or less transmitted rulings of Muhammad al-Shaybani, less authoritative than Zahir al-Riwayah.
المنتقى (al-Muntaqa): A compilation of Hanafi rulings by al-Hakim al-Shahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one purpose of the difficulty of Usul al-Bazdawi?
A) To make the book accessible only to advanced scholars.
B) To exclude pretend scholars and ensure only those worthy engage in ijtihad.
C) To discourage study of usul al-fiqh altogether.
D) To limit the book's readership to Shafi'is only.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Bazdawi is a foundational text that proves Hanafi usul principles with comprehensive evidence, records internal and external debates, and deliberately maintains a high level to ensure only qualified scholars engage in ijtihad.

Al-Bazdawi and al-Sarkhasi: Two Giants of Hanafi Usul
Editorial critique of a description and comparison of two usul works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the works of al-Bazdawi and al-Sarkhasi in terms of difficulty and scholarly reception, and explain the editor's critique of a common description.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi's Usul is famously difficult despite claims of clarity, while al-Sarkhasi's Usul lacks commentaries altogether.

This passage from the editor of Usul al-Bazdawi corrects a superficial description that both works are equally clear. It highlights the scholarly consensus on al-Bazdawi's difficulty and the surprising absence of commentaries on al-Sarkhasi's work. Understanding this helps us appreciate the layered nature of Hanafi usul literature and why certain texts are studied with specific commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two works and their authors
Locate the names Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 483 AH) and al-Sarkhasi (d. 483 AH?), author of al-Mabsut. Note the titles: Usul al-Bazdawi and Usul al-Sarkhasi.
Both are foundational Hanafi usul works from the 5th century AH.
2
Understand the description being critiqued
The editor quotes a description that claims Usul al-Bazdawi is 'easy in expression and concise' and 'the clearest book written in the Hanafi method' and then states that al-Sarkhasi's work is similar in clarity but more expansive.
This description is the target of the editor's criticism.
3
Recognize the editor's counter-argument
The editor rejects this description, pointing to the 'great imams' who wrote commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi and unanimously acknowledged its extreme difficulty, obscure phrases, and hidden symbols.
The editor's authority is based on the consensus of later commentators.
4
Note the comparative point about commentaries and hadith verification
The editor observes that while Usul al-Bazdawi has many commentaries, Usul al-Sarkhasi has none known. Also, recent hadith verification work on al-Sarkhasi's Usul has been done but not yet published.
This indicates a difference in scholarly engagement with the two texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاء بعد هؤلاء فخر الإسلام البزدوي، المتوفى سنة ٤٨٣هـ، وألف كتابه المسمى أصول البزدوي ، وهو كتاب سهل العبارة موجزها ، ويُعَد بحقِّ أوضح كتاب ألف في طريقة الحنفية، ثم جاء السرخسي صاحب المبسوط، وألف كتاباً في الأصول، كان له مثل بيان كتاب البزدوي ولكنه أوسع عبارة، وأكثر تفصيلاً». اهـ
قلت هذا الوصف منه رحمه الله لأصول البزدوي فيه نظر جداً بعد ما تقدم من وصف الأئمة الفحول شراح أصول البزدوي لشدة صعوبة أصول البزدوي ، وإقرارهم بانغلاق عباراته، وخفاء رموزه، وأنه صعب المرام، أبي الزمام.
وفي كلامه رحمه الله تصريح بتقدم البزدوي على السرخسي التأليف.
وأنبه هنا أيضاً في المقارنة إلى نقطة أخرى، وهي أن أصول السرخسي لم يذكر المترجمون أي شرح له أو تعليق، أو حاشية ونحو هذا ويظهر هذا من مراجعة كشف الظنون (۱۱۲/۱ ، حيث ذكره ولم يذكر له أي شرح أو تعليق، وكذلك لم يذكر شيئاً من ذلك محققه الشيخ أبو الوفا الأفغاني رحمه الله في مقدمة تحقيقه له، وكذلك لم أقف في الفهارس على شيء من ذلك، والله أعلم.
- وأذكر هنا أنه تم تخريج أحاديث أصول السرخسي في هذا الزمن من قبل باحثين كريمين في مرحلة الدراسات العليا في جامعة أم القرى بمكة المكرمة، ولم يطبع عملهما بعد، يسر الله لهما ذلك.
And after these came Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, died 483 AH, and authored his book called Usul al-Bazdawi, and it is a book of easy expression and concise, and it is rightfully considered the clearest book written in the Hanafi method. Then came al-Sarkhasi, author of al-Mabsut, and authored a book on usul, which was similar in clarity to al-Bazdawi's book but more expansive in expression and more detailed. End quote. I say: This description of him (may Allah have mercy on him) of Usul al-Bazdawi is highly questionable after what has preceded from the description of the great imams, commentators of Usul al-Bazdawi, regarding the extreme difficulty of Usul al-Bazdawi, and their acknowledgment of the obscurity of its phrases, the hiddenness of its symbols, and that it is difficult to attain, hard to grasp. And in his words (may Allah have mercy on him) is an explicit statement that al-Bazdawi preceded al-Sarkhasi in authorship. And I also point out here in the comparison another point: that al-Sarkhasi's Usul has no mention by biographers of any commentary, gloss, or annotation etc. This is apparent from reviewing Kashf al-Zunun (1/112), where he mentions it and does not mention any commentary or gloss, nor did its editor Sheikh Abu al-Wafa al-Afghani (may Allah have mercy on him) mention anything of that in the introduction to his edition, nor have I found anything in the indexes. And Allah knows best. And I mention here that the hadiths of al-Sarkhasi's Usul have been authenticated in this era by two generous researchers at the graduate level at Umm al-Qura University in Mecca, and their work has not yet been printed; may Allah facilitate that for them.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and critical note from the editor of Usul al-Bazdawi. The editor begins by quoting a description that claims al-Bazdawi's book is easy and clear. He then strongly disagrees, pointing out that the great Hanafi scholars who wrote commentaries on al-Bazdawi's work all acknowledged its extreme difficulty, obscure expressions, and hidden symbols. The editor further notes that this description clearly indicates al-Bazdawi's precedence over al-Sarkhasi in the field. He adds an important observation: while al-Bazdawi's book has many commentaries, al-Sarkhasi's Usul has no known commentaries or glosses, as verified from Kashf al-Zunun and other sources. Finally, he mentions that the hadiths of al-Sarkhasi's Usul have been recently verified by researchers but not yet published. This passage sets the context for why a new edition of al-Bazdawi's work is needed and highlights the esteem in which it is held despite its difficulty.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The foundational work on Hanafi usul al-fiqh by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 483 AH).
أصول السرخسي (Usul al-Sarkhasi): A work on Hanafi usul al-fiqh by al-Sarkhasi (d. 483 AH?), author of al-Mabsut.
كشف الظنون (Kashf al-Zunun): A famous bibliographical encyclopedia by Hajji Khalifa (Kâtip Çelebi), used here to verify the existence of commentaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Al-Bazdawi's work has many commentaries, while al-Sarkhasi's has none.
B) Al-Sarkhasi's work is more difficult than al-Bazdawi's.

Key Takeaway
The editor's note warns against superficial judgments of classical texts; scholarly consensus and commentary history reveal a work's true nature.

The Editor's Methodology for a Critical Edition
Editorial methodology for critical text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the six key steps in the editor's methodology for producing a critical edition of Usul al-Bazdawi and evaluate the rationale behind each step.

Core Idea
Critical editing balances textual fidelity with reader accessibility.

This passage presents the editor's approach to preparing Usul al-Bazdawi. It reveals how a critical edition is constructed: comparing manuscripts, selecting meaningful variants, adding vocalization and punctuation, paragraphing, and handling the author's transitional style. Understanding this methodology will help you better navigate the text and appreciate the scholarly effort behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six editorial tasks
List the six points mentioned: 1) establishing the text from multiple manuscripts, 2) recording only important variant readings, 3) adding moderate vocalization and punctuation, 4) dividing into paragraphs and marking new issues, 5) writing a biography, 6) managing the author's cross-chapter linking phrases.
Each task addresses a specific challenge in presenting a classical text.
2
Analyze the rationale for each task
For each task, ask: why did the editor do this? For example, only important variants are recorded to avoid overwhelming the reader; moderate vocalization clarifies pronunciation without excessive clutter; paragraphing improves readability; preserving the linking phrase as a title respects the author's style.
The editor balances preserving the original with making the text usable.
3
Evaluate the editorial decisions
Consider the strengths and possible drawbacks. For example, does focusing only on important variants risk losing information? Does adding vocalization shape interpretation? The editor's choices reflect a considered methodology.
Think about how you would apply this to another text.
4
Apply the methodology to a hypothetical passage
Imagine you are editing a page from al-Bazdawi. How would you apply each of the six points? For example, mark where you would add vocalization, how you would paragraph, and how you would handle a chapter transition.
This helps internalize the methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهج تحقيق أصول البزدوي
١- أثبتُ ما اجتهدتُ أنه النص الصحيح المختار من خلال النُّسَخ الخطية المتعددة.
٢- لم أُثبت من فوارق النسخ الخطية إلا المهم منها، مما يكون له أثر في المعنى.
٣- ضبطتُ النص ضبطاً متوسطاً، وبخاصة الكلمات المشكلة، وضع علامات الترقيم والتفهيم بين جُمَل الكتاب ومسائله.
٤- جعلت النص مفقراً إلى فقرات وجُمَل ؛ لتقريبه لقارئيه، وجعلت بداية كل مسألة أول السطر ، مع وضع علامات لبدايتها.
من
ه كتبت ترجمةً عن الإمام البزدوي بقدر وسعي، وبما تيسر لي من المراجع التي ذَكَرَتْه ، أو ذكرت ما يتصل به وبمؤلفاته العديدة.
٦ـ من عادة المؤلف رحمه الله أنه في نهاية كل باب يربط السابق باللاحق منه بكلمة أو بعدة كلمات فيقول مثلاً في آخر باب معرفة وجوه الوقوف على أحكام النظم: وهذا باب العزيمة والرخصة»، ثم يبدأ بالكلام عنه من غير إعادة للعنوان وعليه جعلت من منهجي أني أبقيتُ هذه العبارة في آخر الباب السابق، وجعلتها أيضاً عنواناً في الصفحة التي تليها فقلت : باب العزيمة والرخصة إذ هذا هو الأصل في العناوين.
Methodology of editing Usul al-Bazdawi:
1. I established what I strove to be the correct chosen text through multiple manuscript copies.
2. I did not include variant readings from manuscripts except the important ones that affect meaning.
3. I provided moderate vocalization, especially for difficult words, and placed punctuation and explanatory marks between sentences and issues of the book.
4. I divided the text into paragraphs and sentences to bring it closer to its readers, and I placed the beginning of each issue at the start of the line, with marks for its beginning.
5. I wrote a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi to the extent of my ability and what was available to me from references that mentioned him or mentioned what relates to him and his numerous works.
6. It was the habit of the author (may Allah have mercy on him) that at the end of each chapter he would connect the previous to the next with one or several words, for example at the end of the chapter on knowing the ways of understanding the rulings of composition he says: 'And this is the chapter on determination and concession', then he begins discussing it without repeating the title. So I made it my methodology to keep this phrase at the end of the previous chapter and also made it a title on the following page, saying: 'Chapter on determination and concession' for this is the origin in titles.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is the editor's statement of his methodology for the critical edition of Usul al-Bazdawi. It is divided into six points. First, he established the text by comparing multiple manuscripts. Second, he only recorded variant readings that affect the meaning. Third, he added vowel signs and punctuation to aid understanding. Fourth, he paragraphed the text and marked the start of each new issue. Fifth, he wrote a biography of the author. Sixth, he explains how he handled the author's habit of linking chapters with transitional phrases: al-Bazdawi often ended a chapter by announcing the next topic without a separate title, so the editor preserved that phrase at the end of the previous chapter and also used it as the title for the next chapter. This methodology shows a careful approach to presenting a difficult classical text in a user-friendly way while respecting the author's original structure.

Key Terms
ضبط (dabt): The act of adding vowel signs (harakat) to the text to ensure correct pronunciation and reading.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He placed the phrase only in the margin.
D) He rewrote it as a separate heading in both chapters.

Key Takeaway
The editor's careful methodology ensures the text is both authentic and accessible to readers of Usul al-Bazdawi.

The Editor's Method in Usul al-Bazdawi: A Model for Critical Textual Scholarship
Editorial methodology foreword

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the key editorial decisions made in this edition of Usul al-Bazdawi and evaluate their rationale using the principles of textual criticism in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A critical edition balances manuscript evidence, readability, and scholarly apparatus while respecting the author's original structure.

This passage is not a fiqh or usul ruling but the editor's own methodological statement. It reveals how classical texts are transmitted to modern readers. Understanding these choices sharpens your ability to assess the reliability of any edition you use in your studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editorial goals
Read the first and seventh points: the editor aims to establish the correct text from multiple manuscripts and present it clearly. What are the primary and secondary aims?
The primary aim is textual accuracy; secondary is typographic accessibility.
2
Examine the handling of variants
In point two, the editor records only important variants that affect meaning. Why might this be a deliberate choice rather than including all variants?
To avoid overloading the reader, focusing on substantive differences.
3
Analyze the formatting decisions
Points three and four describe vocalization, paragraphing, and issue markers. How do these choices affect the usability of the text?
They make the dense usul text more navigation-friendly.
4
Understand the integration of takhrij
Point ten explains that hadith takhrij by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha is placed alongside the main text. What does this achieve?
It combines the original (asl) with its branch (far'), creating a unified reference.
5
Evaluate the limitation of commentary
Point eight states that the editor rarely adds footnotes due to the book's difficulty. Is this a strength or weakness?
It respects the existing rich commentary tradition and avoids superficial notes.

منهج تحقيق أصول البزدوي
١- أثبتُ ما اجتهدتُ أنه النص الصحيح المختار من خلال النُّسَخ الخطية المتعددة.
٢- لم أُثبت من فوارق النسخ الخطية إلا المهم منها، مما يكون له أثر في المعنى.
٣- ضبطتُ النص ضبطاً متوسطاً، وبخاصة الكلمات المشكلة، وضع علامات الترقيم والتفهيم بين جُمَل الكتاب ومسائله.
٤- جعلت النص مفقراً إلى فقرات وجُمَل؛ لتقريبه لقارئيه، وجعلت بداية كل مسألة أول السطر، مع وضع علامات لبدايتها.
٥- كتبت ترجمةً عن الإمام البزدوي بقدر وسعي، وبما تيسر لي من المراجع التي ذَكَرَتْه، أو ذكرت ما يتصل به وبمؤلفاته العديدة.
٦- من عادة المؤلف رحمه الله أنه في نهاية كل باب يربط السابق باللاحق منه بكلمة أو بعدة كلمات، فيقول مثلاً في آخر باب معرفة وجوه الوقوف على أحكام النظم: "وهذا باب العزيمة والرخصة"، ثم يبدأ بالكلام عنه من غير إعادة للعنوان، وعليه جعلت من منهجي أني أبقيتُ هذه العبارة في آخر الباب السابق، وجعلتها أيضاً عنواناً في الصفحة التي تليها فقلت: باب العزيمة والرخصة إذ هذا هو الأصل في العناوين.
٧- خلال كان قصدي من خدمة هذا الكتاب إثبات نصه الصحيح من النسخ الخطية له، وخدمته من الناحية الطباعية؛ ليكون مشرقاً واضحاً قريباً من طالبيه، وقد انعكس هذا الغرض المهم على سير عملي ومنهجي في خدمته بما يفي بذلك.
٨- لم أكتب في الحواشي أي شرح أو تعليق على الكتاب إلا فيما نَدَر؛ للضرورة، وذلك لأن الصعوبة البالغة في الكتاب تحتاج إلى شرح وتعليق بالجمل والسطور، ولا يكفي لفهمه التعليق اللطيف، وعليه فمَن أراد بغيته منه فعليه الرجوع إلى شروحه وهي متوافرة ولله الحمد، كشرح البابرتي والصغناقي، وعلاء الدين البخاري من المطبوعات، وأما شروحه المخطوطة فالوصول إليها ليس بعسير.
٩- وقد ميّزت تعليقاتي اللطيفة على كل من أصول البزدوي وتخريجه للعلامة قاسم بأني وضعتُ اسمي: سائد: في خاتمة كل منها.
١٠- جمعت بين أصول البزدوي وتخريج أحاديثه للعلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا بين دفتي مجلد واحد؛ جمعاً بين الأصل والفرع، وجعلتُ تخريج كل حديث في مكانه من أصول البزدوي، وبذلك تم وضع الفَصَّ على الخاتم، والقلادة على العنق، وجاء نوراً على نور، ولله الحمد.
Methodology of the editing of Usul al-Bazdawi
1. I have established what I deemed to be the correct, chosen text from among multiple manuscript copies.
2. I did not record from the manuscript variants except the important ones that have an effect on meaning.
3. I applied moderate vocalization, especially to problematic words, and placed punctuation and clarification marks between the sentences of the book and its issues.
4. I divided the text into paragraphs and sentences to bring it closer to its readers, and I placed the beginning of each issue at the start of the line, with markers for its beginning.
5. I wrote a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi to the extent of my ability, and from the references that mentioned him or what relates to him and his numerous works.
6. It is the habit of the author (may Allah have mercy on him) that at the end of every chapter he connects the previous topic with the following one with a word or several words, as he says for example at the end of the chapter on knowing the aspects of stopping at the rulings of the text: "And this is the chapter on determination and license", then he begins speaking about it without repeating the title. Accordingly, I made it part of my methodology that I retained this expression at the end of the previous chapter, and I also made it a title on the following page, saying: "Chapter on determination and license" for this is the basis in titles.
7. During? My intention in serving this book was to establish its correct text from its manuscripts, and to serve it typographically so that it would be bright, clear, and accessible to its students. This important purpose has been reflected in the course of my work and methodology in serving it sufficiently.
8. I did not write in the footnotes any explanation or commentary on the book except rarely, out of necessity, because the extreme difficulty of the book requires explanation and commentary in sentences and lines, and light commentary is not sufficient for understanding it. Accordingly, whoever seeks his desire from it must refer to its commentaries, which are abundant, thank Allah, such as the commentaries of al-Babarti, al-Sighnaqi, and 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari from the published ones. As for its unpublished commentaries, access to them is not difficult.
9. I distinguished my light comments on both Usul al-Bazdawi and its takhrij by 'Allamah Qasim by placing my name: Sa'id at the end of each.
10. I combined Usul al-Bazdawi and the takhrij of its hadiths by 'Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha between the covers of one volume, combining the original and the branch, and I placed the takhrij of each hadith in its place from Usul al-Bazdawi. Thus, the seal was placed on the ring, the necklace on the neck, and light upon light, praise be to Allah.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is the editor's foreword explaining his methodology for producing this edition of Usul al-Bazdawi. He describes a scholarly approach: collating multiple manuscripts to establish a correct text, noting only important variants, applying moderate vocalization, and formatting for readability. He also writes a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi. Regarding the author's habit of linking chapters, the editor preserves the linking phrase and uses it as a title for the next chapter. He states his primary goal is to present a clear, accurate text. He refrains from extensive commentary, citing the book's difficulty and directing readers to existing commentaries like those of al-Babarti, al-Sighnaqi, and al-Bukhari. He marks his own light comments with his name 'Sa'id'. Finally, he combines Usul al-Bazdawi with Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's takhrij of its hadiths into a single volume, arranging the takhrij in its proper place.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): Extraction or verification of hadith sources; here, the work of al-Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha tracing the hadiths cited in Usul al-Bazdawi.
نُسَخ خطية (nusakh khattiyyah): Handwritten manuscript copies of the text used by the editor for collation.
ضبط متوسط (dabt mutawassit): Moderate application of diacritical marks (vocalization) to clarify pronunciation without over-annotation.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The editor of Uṣūl al-Bazdawi prioritized textual accuracy from manuscripts, selective variant recording, and a clean layout while deliberately avoiding extensive footnotes, directing readers to established commentaries.

Evaluating Manuscript Evidence in Usul al-Fiqh Texts
Editor's descriptive catalogue of manuscript witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key features of a manuscript copy and assess its reliability for textual reconstruction in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A manuscript's date, completeness, vocalization, and glosses determine its value for reconstructing the original text.

Before a Hanafi usul text is edited and printed, scholars rely on multiple manuscript copies to determine the most authentic version. The passage you are about to read is a modern editor's catalogue of the manuscripts used for al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul. Each entry provides physical details, textual features, and condition notes—all critical for establishing the textual tradition. Understanding how to parse these descriptions is a foundational skill for anyone engaging deeply with usul al-fiqh sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic codicological data
Note the date (year AH), number of folios (ورقة), lines per page (سطر), and words per line if given. These give a first impression of the copy's age and layout.
Later copies may have different layouts; consistency helps distinguish scribal practices.
2
Evaluate physical completeness
Check for mentions of missing folios (سقط) or partial coverage (e.g., 'first half only'). A complete copy is preferred, but partial copies may preserve superior readings for the sections they contain.
The editor notes missing folios in copies 5 and 8.
3
Assess textual apparatus
Look for vocalization (ضبط الشكل), commentaries (تعليقات), glosses (حواش), and marginal notes. Vocalized copies resolve ambiguity; glosses may indicate scholarly engagement and variant readings.
Copy 5 (800 AH) is praised for vocalization and attributed glosses.
4
Determine provenance and chain
Identify where the manuscript was copied, who owned it, and whether it was collated (قوبل) with an original. These factors affect reliability.
Copy 7 was copied in Ankara at the Madrasa al-Sadriyya; copy 8 ends with a collation statement.
5
Synthesize overall reliability
Combine all features: early date, completeness, vocalization, glosses, and clear provenance. Rank copies for editorial use.
The editor likely used the 800 AH and 815 AH copies as primary witnesses.

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter description of the manuscript copies used by the editor of al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh. It opens with an acknowledgement of a scholar from Konya, Sheikh Muhammad Zahid, who provided several manuscripts. Then follows a numbered list of ten manuscripts, each described by date, number of folios, lines per page, and special features. Details include whether the text is vocalized, presence of commentaries and glosses, marginal notes, attributions, and condition (missing folios, etc.). The editor notes the quality and provenance of each copy, such as a 'royal copy' (نسخة سلطانية) of 815 AH. This bibliographical information is critical for understanding the textual tradition of the work.

Key Terms
نسخة (nuskha): A manuscript copy of a book
ورقة (waraqa): A folio (leaf) of a manuscript
سطر (satar): A line of text on a page
ضبط الشكل (dabt al-shakl): Vocalization of the text (adding vowel marks)
تعليقة (ta'liqa): A commentary note or gloss

Introduction and Front Matter

The Two Types of Knowledge: Foundations of Hanafi Usul
Author's introduction: classification of knowledge and Hanafi theological commitment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Bazdawi's classification of knowledge into theology and jurisprudence, and explain why theology is foundational for Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Knowledge is twofold: theology (tawhid) and jurisprudence (fiqh), with theology as the foundation.

Al-Bazdawi opens his Usul al-Fiqh by establishing the epistemological framework. He divides knowledge into two categories and traces the Hanafi tradition back to Abu Hanifa's theological works. This classification is not merely academic; it determines the starting point for legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author and Text
Recognize that the passage is from al-Bazdawi's 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul', a foundational Hanafi usul text. The author is a major Hanafi jurist-theologian (d. 482 AH).
Al-Bazdawi is part of the Maturidi theological tradition, which frames his usul.
2
State the Two Types of Knowledge
From the first sentence, note that 'knowledge (al-ilm) is of two types: knowledge of tawhid and attributes (theology), and knowledge of fiqh, sacred laws, and rulings (jurisprudence).'
This binary classification is the starting point for all later discussion.
3
Explain the Priority of Theology
Al-Bazdawi says 'the foundation lies in the first type' (al-asl fi al-tanwi' al-awwal). Theology is the basis for jurisprudence, meaning that legal rules derive from theological commitments.
This reflects the Hanafi-Maturidi view that knowledge of God and His attributes precedes legal obligation.
4
Trace the Hanafi Tradition
The author notes that Abu Hanifa authored 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' on theology, affirming the decree of Allah and the creation of human actions. This shows that the Hanafi school has always integrated theology and law.
The reference to 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' is a key identifier of Hanafi theological method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ الإمام الأجل الزاهد أبو الحسن علي بن محمد البزدوي رضوان الله عليه: العلم نوعان: علم التوحيد والصفات، وعلم الفقه والشرائع والأحكام. والأصل في التنويع الأول والمتسكن بالكتاب والسنة [؟] والبداعية والتعلم طريق السنة والجماعة الذي كان عليه الصحابة والتابعون ومشى عليه الصالحون وهو الذي عليه أدركنا من الحنفية رحمهم الله وكان على ذلك سلفنا أصحاب أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد وعلمائهم رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين. وقد صنف أبو حنيفة في ذلك كتاب الفقه الأكبر وأكثر في إثبات القنات [؟] وإثبات تقدير الخير والشر من الله تعالى وأن ذلك بروانين الاستطاعة مع العمل بأن أعمال العباد مخلوقة خلقا [؟] ورد أول ما هن [؟] وكتاب العالم والمتعلم مكانا [؟] بالرسالة وقال...
The Imam, the most learned, the ascetic, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Knowledge is of two types: knowledge of tawhid and attributes, and knowledge of fiqh, sacred laws, and rulings. The foundation lies in the first type, and it is grounded in the Book and the Sunnah... and the non-innovative path, and learning the way of the Sunnah and the community which was followed by the Companions, Successors, and the righteous, and upon which we found the Hanafis, may Allah have mercy on them, and our predecessors, the companions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and their scholars, may Allah be pleased with them all. Abu Hanifa authored in this regard the book 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' and elaborated on affirming [؟] and affirming the decree of good and evil from Allah, and that is [؟] with the capacity along with action, that the deeds of servants are created creation...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This is the opening of al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh, known as Kanz al-Wusul. The author, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, a major Hanafi usuli scholar (d. 482 AH/1089 CE), begins by classifying knowledge into two types: (1) Ilm al-Tawhid (theology) and (2) Ilm al-Fiqh (jurisprudence). He states that the first type is the foundation, and it relies on the Quran and Sunnah, following the path of the Salaf. This division establishes the scope: Usul al-Fiqh deals with the principles derived from the first type to derive the second. He then notes that Imam Abu Hanifa wrote on theology (al-Fiqh al-Akbar) and on predestination, affirming that good and evil are from Allah and that human actions are created by Allah, while humans acquire them. The passage underscores the Hanafi commitment to the Ash'ari-Maturidi theological framework and the necessity of following the Salaf.

Key Terms
العلم (al-ilm): Knowledge, here classified into two types: theology (tawhid) and jurisprudence (fiqh)
علم التوحيد والصفات (ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat): Knowledge of divine unity and attributes, i.e., theology/kalam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Bazdawi's classification establishes that theology (tawhid) precedes jurisprudence (fiqh) in the Hanafi usul tradition.

The Twofold Division of Knowledge and the Hanafi Creedal Foundation
Author's introduction classifying knowledge and affirming Hanafi creed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Al-Bazdawi's classification of knowledge and explain why correct theology is a prerequisite for Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Knowledge is two: creed and law — correct theology is the foundation of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Al-Bazdawi opens his manual of usul al-fiqh with a fundamental classification: knowledge is either theology (ilm al-tawhid) or jurisprudence (ilm al-fiqh). This division is not accidental; it signals that the method of deriving legal rulings is built upon a correct creed. In this lesson, we will unpack this opening statement and see how the Hanafi school grounds its legal theory in the theological principles affirmed by Abu Hanifa in his work Al-Fiqh al-Akbar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Read the Arabic phrase: 'al-ilm nau'an: ilm al-tawhid wa ilm al-fiqh'. State the two types clearly.
Memorize this binary classification; it sets the stage for all later discussions.
2
Determine the foundation of the first type
The author says the first type (theology) is based on the Book, the unanimously agreed Sunnah, and rational proofs. Note that 'aql is included.
This shows Hanafi usul accepts rational evidence, unlike some other schools.
3
Recognize the Hanafi school alignment
Al-Bazdawi states that the path of learning is the path of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, specifically the Hanafi school of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
This is a claim of continuity with the Salaf.
4
Recall the creedal work of Abu Hanifa
The author mentions Al-Fiqh al-Akbar, which affirms faith, divine decree, and the creation of human actions, refuting Qadariyya and Jabriyya.
This book is the creedal basis for Hanafi usul.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم [؟] الحمد لله رب العالمين [؟] والصلاة والسلام على رسول الله [؟]. قال الشيخ الإمام الأجل الزاهد أبو الحسن علي بن محمد البزدوي رحمه الله: العلم نوعان: علم التوحيد وعلم الفقه والشرائع والأحكام. والأصل في التنويع الأول المستند بالكتاب والسنة المجمع عليها [؟] والأدلة العقلية [؟]. والتعلم طريق السنة والجماعة الذي كان عليه الصحابة والتابعون ومشى عليه الصالحون وهو الذي عليه أدركنا من الحنفية رحمهم الله. وكان على ذلك سلفنا: أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف ومحمد رضي الله عنهم أجمعين. وقد صنف أبو حنيفة في ذلك كتاب الفقه الأكبر وأثبت فيه الإيمان والقدر وأثبت تقدير الخير والشر من الله تعالى وأن ذلك يجريان بالاستطاعة مع الفعل بأن أعمال العباد مخلوقة خلقًا حالًا ورد على من خالف ذلك. وقال: ...
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon the Messenger of Allah. The eminent, ascetic Imam, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Knowledge is of two types: knowledge of Tawhid (theology) and knowledge of Fiqh (jurisprudence) and religious laws and rulings. The foundation of the first type is based on the Book and the unanimously agreed upon Sunnah and the rational proofs [?]. And the way of learning is the path of the Sunnah and the community which the Companions and Followers followed and upon which the righteous proceeded, and it is that which we found our Hanafi scholars upon, may Allah have mercy on them. And our predecessors were upon that: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, may Allah be pleased with them all. And Abu Hanifa compiled on that the book Al-Fiqh al-Akbar and established in it faith and divine decree, and he established the predestination of good and evil from Allah Almighty, and that they occur with capacity along with the action, and that the actions of servants are created in a state of creation, and he refuted those who opposed that. And he said: ...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This is the opening of Al-Bazdawi's Usul, establishing the author's approach. He begins by stating that knowledge is of two fundamental types: 'ilm al-tawhid (theology, i.e., beliefs or usul al-din) and 'ilm al-fiqh (jurisprudence, i.e., practical legal rulings). This division is typical in Hanafi works to show that fiqh is built upon correct creed. He then asserts that the foundation of the first type (theology) is based on the Qur'an, the widely transmitted Sunnah, and rational proofs—indicating that Hanafi usul accepts 'aql as a source. The 'way of learning' he refers to is the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, which the Salaf (Companions, Followers) followed. He explicitly states that the Hanafi school (ashabuna al-hanafiyya) adheres to this path. He praises the three great imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. He then notes that Abu Hanifa authored Al-Fiqh al-Akbar on creedal matters, affirming iiman (faith), qadar (divine decree), and the creation of human actions—a stance against the Qadariyya and Jabriyya. This passage shows that usul al-fiqh in the Hanafi tradition is not isolated from theology; rather, it presupposes a specific theological framework.

Key Terms
علم التوحيد (ilm al-tawhid): The knowledge of divine unity and creedal beliefs, including faith, divine attributes, and predestination.
علم الفقه (ilm al-fiqh): Knowledge of legal rulings derived from detailed evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One type: only Fiqh
B) Two types: Tawhid and Fiqh
C) Three types: Tawhid, Fiqh, and Hadith
D) Four types: Tawhid, Fiqh, Usul, and Tafsir

Key Takeaway
Al-Bazdawi's twofold division reminds us that Hanafi usul is rooted in a specific creedal framework, with theology as the bedrock of legal methodology.

The Scholarly Output of a Hanafi Faqih: A Biographical Window
Biographical list of scholar's works

Learning Objective

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's works span multiple sciences, showing the integrated nature of Hanafi ilm.

This passage presents a list of 35 works attributed to a Hanafi scholar, likely appended by a commentator of Usul al-Bazdawi. The list is a window into the scholarly output of the Hanafi tradition, covering defenses of Abu Hanifa, hadith verification, usul al-fiqh, and more. Understanding the range of these works helps us appreciate the breadth and depth of Hanafi scholarship, especially the emphasis on defending foundational positions and engaging with primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list for thematic clusters
Look for groups of works with similar titles such as 'Ajwiba' (defenses), 'Takhrij' (hadith verification), 'Hashiya' (commentaries), etc. This will reveal the main areas of the author's focus.
For instance, works 2-5 are all defenses; works 12-22 are mostly takhrij works.
2
Identify the core Hanafi disciplines
Determine which works belong to fiqh, usul al-fiqh, hadith, and other sciences. Note the presence of works on Hanafi usul (e.g., work 32) and tarjih (work 24).
3
Recognise the defensive genre
Works 2-5 are explicitly titled 'al-Ajwiba' (answers) addressing objections against Imam Abu Hanifa or Hanafi usul. Consider why such a genre was important in the Hanafi tradition.
These defenses indicate a polemical context where Hanafi positions were being challenged.
4
Reflect on the role of biographical lists
Understand that such lists serve to establish scholarly authority, showcase mastery, and provide a map for students to trace the development of Hanafi thought.
The list itself is a form of taqriz (praise) and a guide to further study.

The list demonstrates the scholarly output of a prolific Hanafi author engaged in both original composition and critical commentary. The mention of works like 'al-Ajwiba 'ala I'tiradat al-Bukhari' indicates engagement with intra-madhhab critique, while 'Hashiya 'ala al-Talwih' shows interaction with the later Hanafi usul tradition. The passage is front matter, likely part of an introductory biography preceding the main text of Usul al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The scholarly process of tracing a hadith to its original source, verifying its chain and grading.
أجوبة (ajwiba): Answers or responses; in this context, works that refute objections against Imam Abu Hanifa or Hanafi positions.
حاشية (hashiya): A marginal commentary or gloss on a primary text, often expanding or refining the original commentary.

The Scholarly Legacy of a Hanafi Master: Bibliography and Biography
Lists over 40 works of a Hanafi scholar and records his death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the range of a Hanafi scholar's works across multiple Islamic disciplines and explain how his authorship contributed to the preservation and development of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A scholar's bibliography reveals his madhhab's priorities and his own intellectual range.

This passage presents the bibliography of a prolific Hanafi scholar, listing dozens of works on hadith, fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and other sciences. Such biographical records are crucial for understanding the transmission and evolution of Hanafi legal thought. By studying the titles, we can trace which classical texts were considered important enough to have commentaries, critical editions (takhrij), or super-commentaries (hashiya), and how the scholar engaged with the madhhab's foundational works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's disciplines
Scan the list of works and note which Islamic sciences are represented: hadith (e.g., Takhrij works, Hashiya on Mashariq al-Anwar), fiqh (e.g., Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi), and usul al-fiqh (e.g., Hashiya on al-Talwih). This shows the scholar was a multi-disciplinary authority.
Many works are commentaries (sharh) or critical annotations (hashiya), indicating interaction with earlier texts.
2
Categorize works by type
Classify the titles into types: Takhrij (hadith source verification), Sharh (commentary), Hashiya (gloss), and original compositions (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Qasimiyya). Notice the prevalence of Takhrij and Hashiya, reflecting a concern for hadith authenticity and textual precision.
Takhrij works verify the hadith sources for popular Sufi or fiqh texts, showing integration of hadith criticism with later works.
3
Relate works to Hanafi school needs
Identify which works directly serve Hanafi fiqh and usul: e.g., 'al-Tarjih wa al-Tashih ala Mukhtasar al-Quduri' is a work of preference and correction on a key Hanafi matn; 'Hashiya ala al-Talwih' is a gloss on a major Hanafi usul work. These indicate active development of madhhab doctrine.
Works on ikhtilaf (e.g., Sharh Durar al-Bihar fi Ikhtilaf al-Madhhahib al-Arba'a) show engagement with comparative fiqh.
4
Note the historical context of death
Record the death date (Rabi' al-Akhar 879 AH) and place (Cairo). This situates the scholar in the late 9th century AH, a period of rich Hanafi scholarship in Egypt.
The detailed death notice with prayer reflects the biographer's respect and the importance of the scholar in the tradition.

وهكذا بعد عُمر عامرٍ بالعلم والعمل والسماع والتدريس والإقراء والإفتاء والتأليف والنشاط والحيوية والرحلة في طلب العلم، ونَفْع الخاصة والعامة والإبداع العلمي مع التحقيق والتدقيق فيه، ومع كريم الأخلاق العالية والسجايا الطيبة العطرة والتواضع الجم، وقد عاش سبعاً وسبعين سنة، بعد هذا انتقل إلى رحمة الله ليلة الخميس، رابع ربيع الآخر، سنة ٨٧٩هـ ، ودُفن بالقاهرة، رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه، الأنبياء والصديقين والشهداء والصالحين.
وجعله مع
18 - Takhrij ahadith 'Awarif al-Ma'arif' by al-Suhrawardi. 19 - Takhrij ahadith 'al-Fara'id' by al-Sajawandi. 20 - Takhrij ahadith 'Minhaj al-'Abidin' by al-Ghazali. 21 - Takhrij 'Awali al-Qadi Bakkar'. 22 - Takhrij 'Awali al-Layth ibn Sa'd'. 23 - Tarajim Mashayikh al-Mashayikh. 24 - al-Tarjih wa al-Tashih 'ala Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 25 - Tarsi' al-Jawhar al-Naqi by Ibn al-Turkumani. 26 - al-Ta'rif wa al-Ikbar bi Takhrij Ahadith al-Ikhtiyar by al-Mawsili. 27 - Taqwim al-Lisan fi al-Du'afa'. 28 - Talkhis al-Sira al-Nabawiyya by Mughultay. 29 - al-Thiqat mimman lam yaqa' fi al-Kutub al-Sitta. 30 - Hashiya 'ala Sharh Alfiyyat al-'Iraqi. 31 - Hashiya 'ala Sharh Mukhtasar al-Manar by Ibn Malik. 32 - Hashiya 'ala al-Talwih li al-Taftazani fi Usul al-Fiqh al-Hanafi. 33 - Hashiya 'ala Mashariq al-Anwar li al-Saghani fi al-Hadith. 34 - Risala fi Sihhat al-Salat bi al-Qira'at al-'Ashr. 35 - Sharh Durar al-Bihar fi Ikhtilaf al-Madhhahib al-Arba'a by al-Qunawi. 36 - Sharh Fara'id al-Sajawandi. 37 - Sharh Kitab Jami' al-Masanid by al-Khwarizmi. 38 - Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi fi al-Furu'. 39 - Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. 40 - al-Fatawa al-Qasimiyya (his fatwas). 41 - al-Kafa'a fi al-Nikah. 42 - Man Rawa 'an Abihi 'an Jaddihi. 43 - Mujibat al-Ahkam wa Waqi'at al-Ayyam. 44 - Nuzhat al-Ra'id fi Adillat al-Fara'id. And other important books full of rare benefits whose existence is rare elsewhere. His death, may Allah have mercy on him: And thus, after a life full of knowledge, action, listening, teaching, dictation, giving fatwas, authorship, activity, vitality, and travel in seeking knowledge, benefiting the elite and general public, and scientific creativity with investigation and precision, and with noble high morals, good fragrant nature, and great humility. He lived seventy-seven years, then moved to the mercy of Allah on the night of Thursday, 4th Rabi' al-Akhar, year 879 AH, and was buried in Cairo. May Allah have mercy on him and raise his station, and make him with the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note listing over forty works attributed to a Hanafi scholar, followed by an account of his death. The list includes works on hadith (takhrij, hashya), fiqh (sharh, mukhtasar), and usul al-fiqh, indicating the scholar's broad expertise. The biography emphasizes his lifelong dedication to ilm ('knowledge'), amal ('action'), samaa' ('listening to hadith'), tadris ('teaching'), ifta' ('giving fatwas'), and ta'lif ('authorship'). His death is recorded in 879 AH, and he was buried in Cairo. The passage closes with a prayer that Allah join him with the prophets, truthful, martyrs, and righteous. This type of biographical entry is common in the colophons of classical works, where the copyist or editor briefly notes the author's life and works.

The biography and bibliography of a Hanafi scholar provide essential context for understanding the development and transmission of the madhhab's texts and doctrines.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Precision of Hadith Wording in Usul al-Fiqh
Editor explains his method for hadith extraction and describes two manuscript copies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why multiple hadith sources may differ in wording and apply the editor's approach to identify the closest wording for usul analysis.

Core Idea
In usul al-fiqh, the exact wording of a hadith matters — editors use closest wording when the original is not found.

This lesson explores the editor's methodology for handling hadiths in Usul al-Bazdawi. You will learn how hadith extraction accounts for variation in wording across sources and why this is critical for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The editor states that when Imam al-Bazdawi does not find the exact wording of a hadith, he uses the closest wording and indicates that. Recognize that this is a common scenario in hadith extraction.
The exact wording is crucial for legal reasoning (istidlal).
2
Understand the editor's method
The editor warns that citing multiple sources does not guarantee uniform wording; copies of a single book may differ. He emphasizes noting this variation.
Examples: Jami' al-Usul, al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib.
3
Recognize the implication for usul
When a hadith is used as a dalil in usul, the precise wording can affect the meaning (e.g., amm vs khass). The editor's method ensures we work with the closest available wording.
This is part of tahqiq al-manat.
4
Note the grading practice
The author usually grades the hadith (sahih, da'if, etc.), but sometimes does not. This affects the weight of the evidence.
Grading is part of evaluating thubut and dalala.
