الأحاديث والآثار المخرجة إلى (٢٠١٦) حديثاً.
٩- إذا لم يجد المؤلف نص الحديث المذكور في أصول البزدوي الذي يريد تخريجه : فإنه يأتي بأقرب الألفاظ إليه، ويشير إلى ذلك. وأنبه هنا إلى قضية مهمة جداً في تخريج أحاديث الكتاب بشكل عام، وتخريج اللفظ نفسه الذي ذكره مؤلف الكتاب الإمام البزدوي، فالمخرج للحديث يذكر أحياناً عشرة مصادر للحديث أو أكثر، ولا شك أن هذه أصول الحديثية التي عزى إليها المخرج ليست متحدة في لفظ الحديث، بل قد تختلف نُسَخُ الكتاب الواحد وهذا طبيعي جدا حاصل في كل الكتب التي تُعنى بالتخريج وعزو الحديث إلى الأصول، وعلى رأسها: جامع الأصول لابن الأثير، والترغيب والترهيب للمنذري، والجامع الصغير للسيوطي، ونحوها ، وهو أمر يجب أن يتنبه إليه.
١٠ - يبين المؤلف في الغالب درجة الحديث وحكمه فيه، وفي أحيان أخرى لا يذكر شيئاً.
١١ - للكتاب نسختان إحداهما بخط المؤلف، بتاريخ ٨٥٩هـ، ونسخة أخرى بخط تلميذ المؤلف محمد بن عمران الحنفي، بتاريخ ٨٦٤هـ، وفيها بلاغات بالمقابلة، وفي آخرها بخط المؤلف: أنه قرأ الكتاب عليه تلميذه الناسخ، وأنه أجازه بروايته عنه.
والذي توصلتُ إليه من خلال مقابلة النسختين أن المؤلف في نسخة التلميذ قد صقل الكتاب وحرَّره حين قرأه عليه، وغيّر في بعض ألفاظه، وأضاف فيه زيادات على نسخته التي هي بخط يده، ومَلاً بعض البياضات التي تركها في نسخته ،وهذا كله يجعل نسخة التلميذ المجاز بها هي النسخة المعدلة المحررة المعتمدة، والله أعلم.
۱۲ - يترك المؤلف أحياناً ـ والنسخة بخطه - بياضاً يتفاوت غالباً سطر أو أقل أو أكثر عند تخريج حديث ما، وذلك غالباً عند عدم وقوفه على تخريجه، فلعله يقف عليه فيما بعد، وقد حصل مثل هذا، ففي نسخته التي هي بخطه بيض لبعض الأحاديث، وأعاد وحين قراءة الكتاب في نسخة تلميذه قراءة تحرير وإتقان ملأ بعض تلك البياضات، وتَرَكَ الباقي مما لم يقف والله أعلم.
The hadiths and athar extracted (2016 hadiths). 9- If the author does not find the text of the hadith mentioned in Usul al-Bazdawi that he wishes to extract, then he brings the closest wording to it, and indicates that. And I draw attention here to a very important issue regarding the extraction of hadiths of the book in general, and the extraction of the exact wording mentioned by the author Imam al-Bazdawi. The extractor of the hadith sometimes mentions ten or more sources for the hadith, and there is no doubt that these hadith sources to which the extractor refers are not uniform in the wording of the hadith; rather, the copies of a single book may differ, and this is very natural and occurs in all books concerned with extraction and attribution of hadith to sources, foremost among them: Jami' al-Usul by Ibn al-Athir, al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib by al-Mundhiri, al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Suyuti, and the like, and this is something that must be noted. 10- The author mostly indicates the grade of the hadith and his ruling on it, and sometimes he does not mention anything. 11- The book has two copies: one in the author's handwriting, dated 859 AH, and another copy in the handwriting of the author's student Muhammad ibn 'Imran al-Hanafi, dated 864 AH, which contains collation notes, and at the end in the author's handwriting: that his student the copyist read the book to him, and that he authorized him to narrate it from him. What I have concluded through comparing the two copies is that the author, in the student's copy, refined and edited the book when the student read it to him, changed some of its wording, added additions to his copy that is in his own handwriting, and filled in some blanks he had left in his copy. All of this makes the student's authorized copy the revised, edited, and authoritative copy, and Allah knows best. 12- The author sometimes — in his own copy — leaves a blank space, usually varying a line or less or more, when extracting a hadith, often when he has not come across its extraction, perhaps he will come across it later. This has happened: in his own copy, he left blanks for some hadiths. Then, when the book was read in his student's copy with a reading of revision and accuracy, he filled some of those blanks, and left the rest of what he had not found, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction, describing his methodology in extracting hadiths for the book and the manuscript situation. The editor notes that when Imam al-Bazdawi does not find the exact wording of a hadith, he uses the closest wording and indicates that. The editor warns that hadith extraction often cites multiple sources which may differ in wording, a common issue in hadith compilation works. He states that the author usually grades the hadith, but sometimes does not. He then describes two manuscript copies: one by the author (859 AH) and another by the author's student (864 AH) with collation notes and an ijaza. By comparing them, the editor concludes that the student's copy is the revised and authoritative version, as the author made changes and filled blanks during the student's reading. Finally, the editor notes that the author left blanks in his own copy where he had not found a hadith's source, and later filled some of them in the student's copy.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The process of extracting a hadith from its primary sources and citing its chains and locations.
نسخة (nuskha): A manuscript copy of a book.
إجازة (ijaza): Permission to transmit a book or knowledge, given by a scholar to a student.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the editor consider the student's copy (dated 864 AH) as the authoritative version?
A) It is older than the author's copy.
B) The author personally revised and added to it during a reading session.
C) It contains more hadiths than the author's copy.
D) The student was more reliable than the author.

Key Takeaway
Precision in hadith wording is essential in usul al-fiqh, and editors use careful methods to handle variation.

Determining the Authoritative Manuscript: A Lesson in Hanafi Textual Criticism
Editor describes two manuscript copies and explains why the student's copy is authoritative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare two manuscript versions and state which is considered authoritative based on authorial revision and ijaza.

Core Idea
The student's copy with authorial revisions and ijaza becomes the authoritative version.

This lesson examines the two manuscript copies of Usul al-Bazdawi and the editor's reasoning for preferring the student's copy. You will learn how textual criticism is done in the Hanafi tradition, particularly when the author himself revises and authorizes a copy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manuscripts
There is the author's copy (859 AH) and the student's copy (864 AH). Note the dates and the relationship: the student copied the book and read it to the author.
The student's copy contains an ijaza at the end.
2
Examine the evidence of revision
The editor found that in the student's copy, the author made changes, added additions, and filled blanks that were left in his own copy. This indicates the author actively edited the text during the reading.
Blanks were left when the author hadn't found a source; he filled some later.
3
Understand the concept of ijaza
The author wrote at the end that he read the book with the student and permitted him to narrate it. This ijaza authenticates the student's copy as a transmission from the author.
Ijaza is a key element in establishing the reliability of a manuscript.
4
Conclude the authoritative status
Based on the revisions and ijaza, the student's copy is the 'revised, edited, and authoritative' version. The author's own copy, though in his handwriting, is earlier and less complete.
This principle applies to other Hanafi texts as well.

Editor's Methodology for Hadith Verification in Usul al-Bazdawi
Editorial methodology statement for hadith verification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key steps in the editor's methodology for hadith verification and explain the rationale behind each editorial decision.

Core Idea
Critical editions rely on manuscript comparison and source verification—editorial choices directly affect textual authority.

When studying classical Hanafi usul texts like Usul al-Bazdawi, understanding the editor's methodology helps you assess the reliability of the printed text. This lesson unpacks the procedures used in a modern critical edition, showing how textual integrity is preserved while balancing readability and scholarly rigor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philological tools
The editor used multiple manuscripts: the student's copy read to the author (with ijazah) and the author's autograph, plus original hadith sources. Recognize these as standard tools for verifying transmission.
Ijazah confirms authorized transmission – a key concept in Hanafi riwayah.
2
Analyze the rationale for each editorial decision
Silent correction of slips, omission of variant notes, and concise hadith references all aim to avoid overloading the book while ensuring correctness. Consider the balance between scholarly completeness and practical usability.
The editor prioritized a single-volume edition for accessibility.
3
Connect to broader Hanafi textual scholarship
This methodology reflects principles of hadith criticism and textual transmission (riwayah) that underpin Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The editor's reliance on authorized copies mirrors the emphasis on authentic chains (sanad).
Takhrij is rooted in the Hanafi tradition of verifying proofs.
4
Evaluate the impact on textual reliability
By comparing multiple witnesses and consulting original sources, the editor increases confidence in the text. Silent corrections, however, require trust in the editor's expertise—a trade-off with transparency.
Modern readers should be aware of these editorial choices.

منهج تحقيق تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي
۱ - اعتمدت نسخةً تلميذ المؤلف التي قرأها عليه، وفي آخرها إجازة له بها، كما تقدم بيان ذلك، مع مقارنتها بنسخة المؤلف التي هي بخطه، التأكد أيضاً بمراجعة الأصول الحديثية التي عُزي إليها الحديث. ۲- جعلتُ تخريج كل حديث في موضعه من أصول البزدوي الذي أكرمني الله بخدمته أيضاً، وذلك لتتم الفائدة منه في الحال. ٣- لم أعلّق على الكتاب إلا في حالات نادرة، مثل ما فعلتُ في أصول البزدوي، إذ كان قصدي الأول هو إخراج نص الكتاب مفرغاً في مكانه من كتاب أصول البزدوي. -٣- تبيَّن لي من خلال خدمة النص ومراجعة الأصول التي يوجد فيها الحديث تبين أحياناً سَبْقُ قلم في النُّسَخ الخطية، أو سقوط كلمة يتم بها المعنى، أو خطأ في بعض الألفاظ، وعليه فكنتُ أُثبت الصواب بعد التحري، دون الإشارة إلى ذلك؛ خشية إثقال الحواشي. ٤- كنتُ إذا بيض المؤلف موضعَ تخريج حديث ما : أقوم بالبحث عن تخريجه بما تيسر لي، فإن وجدتُ شيئاً : أحيل إليه باختصار، مع الإشارة إلى ذلك، وإلا تركت البياض على حاله. -٥- ضبطتُ ما اشتبه من الألفاظ وأسماء الرواة والأماكن بالرجوع إلى كتب أهل الشأن في ذلك. ٦- لم أُشر إلى فوارق نسخة المؤلف عن نسخة التلميذ، بعداً عن إثقال الحواشي، وفي الحقيقة والواقع أن نسخة التلميذ هي نسخة للمؤلف أيضاً، وذلك بقراءتها عليه وتحريره لها، وإجازته له بها بخطه. كذلك لم أقم بإثبات الجزء والصفحة للمصادر التي عزى إليها المؤلف ؛ بُعداً عن تكبير حجم الكتاب بما هو متيسر في هذا الزمن جداً، وليَخرج أصول البزدوي وتخريجه بين دفتي مجلد واحد؛ تقريباً له بين أيدي القراء الكرام. ترجمت للعلامة قاسم ترجمةً متوسطة غير مطولة؛ وذلك لتكرر ترجمته في مقدمات محققي كتبه.
Methodology for verifying hadith of Usul al-Bazdawi
1. I relied on the copy of the author's student which he read to him, and at the end of which is a license (ijazah) from him for it, as previously mentioned, comparing it with the author's copy which is in his own handwriting, and also verifying by consulting the hadith sources to which the hadith was attributed. 2. I placed the verification of each hadith in its location in Usul al-Bazdawi, which Allah also honored me to serve, so that the benefit may be complete at once. 3. I did not comment on the book except in rare cases, as I did in Usul al-Bazdawi, since my primary aim was to produce the text of the book in its place from the book Usul al-Bazdawi. -3. Through serving the text and reviewing the sources in which the hadith is found, it sometimes became clear to me that there was a slip of the pen in the manuscript copies, or a missing word by which the meaning is completed, or an error in some wording. Accordingly, I would record the correct version after investigation, without indicating it, for fear of overloading the footnotes. 4. When the author left blank a place for verifying a particular hadith, I would search for its verification as far as I could. If I found something, I would refer to it briefly, pointing it out, otherwise I left the blank as it was. -5. I corrected what was ambiguous in wording and names of narrators and places by referring to the books of the specialists in that. 6. I did not indicate the differences between the author's copy and the student's copy, to avoid overloading the footnotes, and in truth and reality the student's copy is also a copy of the author, because he read it to him, corrected it, and licensed it to him in his own handwriting. Likewise, I did not include the part and page numbers for the sources to which the author referred, to avoid enlarging the book with what is very easily accessible in this age, and so that Usul al-Bazdawi and its verification may come out between the covers of one volume, making it accessible to the gracious readers. I wrote a moderate, not lengthy, biography of al-Allamah Qasim, because his biography is repeated in the introductions of editors of his books.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is the editor's methodology statement for the critical edition of Usul al-Bazdawi. The editor explains his approach to verifying hadith citations: he primarily relied on the student's copy read to the author, compared it with the author's autograph, and checked the original hadith sources. He placed each hadith verification within the text for immediate benefit. He only added rare marginal notes, preferring to correct errors silently to avoid heavy footnotes. When the author left blanks for hadith verification, he searched and referenced briefly or left blank. He corrected ambiguous words and names using specialist works. He did not note differences between the two copies because the student's copy was effectively an authorized version. He also omitted modern page/volume references for brevity, aiming for a single-volume edition. Finally, he included a moderate biography of the author, al-Allamah Qasim, since it appears in other editions. This methodology reflects standard scholarly editorial practice in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The process of verifying and tracing the sources of hadith in original collections.
نسخة المؤلف (nuskhat al-mu'allif): The original manuscript written by the author himself.
إجازة (ijazah): A formal license from a scholar authorizing a student to transmit his work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the editor choose not to indicate differences between the author's copy and the student's copy?
A) Because he considered the student's copy also an authorized version of the author.
B) Because the differences were too minor to mention.
C) Because he wanted to save space in the edition.
D) Because he did not have access to the author's copy.

Key Takeaway
Critical editions of Hanafi usul texts require careful manuscript comparison and hadith verification; editorial choices like silent corrections are made to balance textual integrity with usability.

The Manuscript Basis of Usool al-Bazdawi
Editorial description of manuscripts and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two primary manuscripts of Takhreej Usool al-Bazdawi and explain why the student's copy holds authorial authority.

Core Idea
A student's copy read back and approved by the author is as authoritative as the author's autograph.

Critical editions of classical Hanafi usul texts rely on surviving manuscripts. In this lesson, we examine the two manuscripts used for the critical edition of 'Kanz al-Wusul' by al-Bazdawi: the author's own holograph and a copy made by his student with personal authorization. Understanding their provenance is essential for assessing the reliability of the text we study today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the manuscripts
From the source, note that there are two manuscripts: one in the author's handwriting (dated 859 AH) and one in the student's handwriting (dated 864 AH). Locate their current repositories: Tarim, Yemen and Cairo, Egypt.
The student's copy is not a mere transcription; it was collated with the author.
2
Understand the authorization process
The student's copy contains collation notes and a written ijazah (authorization) in the author's own hand, stating that the student read the text back to him and he approved its transmission.
This gives the student's copy an authority equal to the autograph.
3
Evaluate the chain of transmission
Consider that the student's copy bridges the author to later readers through a direct, verified link. Both manuscripts together provide a solid foundation for the critical edition.
The editor considers both copies authoritative, so variants between them are minimal.

كذلك لم أقم بإثبات الجزء والصفحة للمصادر التي عزى إليها المؤلف ؛ بُعداً عن تكبير حجم الكتاب بما هو متيسر في هذا الزمن جداً، وليَخرج أصول البزدوي وتخريجه بين دفتي مجلد واحد؛ تقريباً له إلى أيدي القراء الكرام۔
ترجمت للعلامة قاسم ترجمةً متوسطة غير مطولة؛ وذلك لتكرر ترجمته في مقدمات محققي كتبه.

نسخ تخريج أصول البزدوي المعتمدة في التحقيق
للكتاب نسختان نفيستان :إحداهما بخط المؤلف، بتاريخ ٨٥٩هـ، والنسخة الثانية بخط تلميذ المؤلف محمد بن عمران الحنفي، بتاريخ ٨٦٤هـ، وفيها بلاغات بالمقابلة مع المؤلف وفي آخرها بخط المؤلف: أنه قرأه عليه تلميذه الناسخ، وأجازه بروايته عنه.
وأصل نسخة المؤلف مودَعةٌ في مكتبة الأحقاف في مدينة تريم من اليمن السعيد في مجموعة آل يحيى برقم (٣٥)، وعدد أوراقها (٦١) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة منها ۲۱ سطراً، وتاريخ كتابتها سنة ٨٥٩هـ، وقد صورتها مباشرة عن طريق مدير المكتبة هناك.
وأما النسخة الثانية : فهي نسخة تلميذ المؤلف، وأصلها محفوظ دار الكتب المصرية بالقاهرة برقم (١٤٣٧) ، وعدد أوراقها (٥٣) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ۱۹ سطراً.

-١ - طبع تخريج أصول البزدوي طبعةً حجرية عليلة سقيمة في حاشية أصول البزدوي ، ونُشرت هذه الطبعة في كراتشي بباكستان، الناشر: مير محمد کتب خانة، بدون تاريخ.
٢- كما تم تحقيقه في رسالة دكتوراه في جامعة كراتشي، كلية
The people of expertise have written on that. 81 -6- I did not point out the differences between the author's copy and the student's copy, in order to avoid overburdening the footnotes. In reality, the student's copy is also a copy of the author, because it was read back to him, revised by him, and he authorized its transmission in his own handwriting. Likewise, I did not provide the volume and page numbers for the sources cited by the author, to avoid enlarging the book beyond what is easily manageable in this age, so that Usool al-Bazdawi and its Takhreej appear between the covers of a single volume, making it accessible to the respected readers. I wrote a moderate-length biography of Allamah Qasim, not lengthy, because his biography is repeated in the introductions of editors of his books. 82 Copies of Takhreej Usool al-Bazdawi used in the critical edition. The book has two precious manuscripts: one in the author's handwriting, dated 859 AH, and the second in the handwriting of the author's student Muhammad ibn Imran al-Hanafi, dated 864 AH. In it (the student's copy) are collation notes with the author, and at the end in the author's handwriting: that his student, the copyist, read it to him, and he authorized him to transmit it from him. The original of the author's copy is deposited in the Al-Ahqaf Library in the city of Tarim in blessed Yemen, in the Al-Yahya collection, under number (35). It has 61 folios, each page 21 lines, and its date of writing is 859 AH. I directly photographed it through the director of the library there. As for the second copy, it is the author's student's copy, its original is preserved in the Egyptian National Library in Cairo, under number (1437). It has 53 folios, each page 19 lines. Editions of the book: -1- Takhreej Usool al-Bazdawi was lithographically printed, a defective and weak print in the margin of Usool al-Bazdawi, published in Karachi, Pakistan, publisher: Mir Muhammad Kutub Khana, undated. -2- It was also edited in a PhD thesis at the University of Karachi, Faculty...
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction to the critical edition of Usool al-Bazdawi (the text of 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul' by al-Bazdawi). The editor explains his editorial decisions: he deliberately omits recording variant readings between the author's holograph and the student's copy to keep footnotes concise, noting that the student's copy effectively holds authorial authority because it was read back to the author and personally approved. He also refrains from providing volume/page references for sources to keep the edition compact. The editor then describes the two manuscripts used: the author's autograph (dated 859 AH, held in Tarim, Yemen) and a student copy (dated 864 AH, in Cairo). The student copy contains collation notes and the author's written authorization. Finally, he lists previous editions: a defective lithograph in Karachi and a PhD thesis edition from the University of Karachi. This front matter is typical of critical editions of classical Hanafi usul works.

Key Terms
نسخة المؤلف (nuskhat al-mu'allif): The author's own handwritten copy (autograph).
إجازة (ijazah): Written authorization from a teacher to transmit a text.
مقابلة (muqabalah): Collation: comparing the copy with the original to ensure accuracy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The critical edition of Usool al-Bazdawi relies on two manuscripts, both authoritative due to the author's direct involvement.

Editorial Methodology in Hanafi Textual Criticism
Editorial description of manuscripts and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the editorial decisions described in the introduction of a Hanafi usul critical edition.

Core Idea
Critical editions balance scholarly detail with accessibility; each omission is a reasoned choice.

The editor of Usool al-Bazdawi made deliberate decisions to omit variant notes and source references, and to include a moderate biography. These choices reflect a methodology aimed at producing a usable edition for a wide readership. Understanding this methodology helps you critically engage with any printed text of classical Hanafi works.

Guided Path
1
Identify editorial decisions
List the three main decisions: (1) not pointing out variants between the two manuscripts, (2) not providing volume/page references for cited sources, (3) writing a moderate biography rather than an extensive one.
Each decision is justified in the text.
2
Understand the rationale
For each decision, find the editor's justification: avoiding overburdening footnotes, keeping the book compact and accessible, and avoiding repetition of existing biographies.
The editor prioritizes the reader's convenience and the single-volume format.
3
Assess the impact
Consider how these decisions affect a student's experience and the scholarly value of the edition. Are there trade-offs?
Missing variants may hide textual nuances, but the edition gains readability.

Introducing Usul al-Bazdawi: A Cornerstone of Hanafi Usul
Title page of a Hanafi usul al-fiqh classic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the title, author, and accompanying work of Usul al-Bazdawi and explain its significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The title page of Usul al-Bazdawi introduces a cornerstone of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, paired with a critical hadith takhrij.

This lesson examines the title page of a foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. While it contains no legal rulings, it provides essential bibliographic context that will anchor your study of the work. You will learn to identify the key figures and understand the structure of this edition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main title and its translation
Locate the full Arabic title 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul' and its meaning 'The Treasure of Arriving at Knowledge of the Principles'. This is the name of the book.
The shorter title 'Usul al-Bazdawi' is commonly used.
2
Note the author and his dates
The author is Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi (400–482 AH). Recognize that he is a major Hanafi usul scholar.
His death date places him in the 5th century AH.
3
Note the accompanying work and its author
The edition includes 'Takhrīj Aḥādīth Uṣūl al-Bazdawī' by Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi (579–802 AH). This work verifies the hadiths cited by al-Bazdawi.
The takhrij is a critical scholarly tool.
4
Understand the role of the editor
The text was edited by Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. Modern editions often include editorial work to ensure accuracy.
5
Reflect on why this page matters
The title page confirms you are studying a reliable edition of an authoritative Hanafi usul text. Knowing the chain of authorship and scholarship reinforces trust in the content.
Always check the title page when beginning a new text.

Usul al-Bazdawi: The Treasure of Arriving at Knowledge of the Principles. By Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi (400-482 AH), may Allah have mercy on him. With it: Takhrīj Aḥādīth Uṣūl al-Bazdawī, by the Imam, the Allama, Qāsim ibn Quṭlūbughā al-Ḥanafī (579-802 AH), may Allah have mercy on him. Edited by Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This is the title page of the book 'Usul al-Bazdawi' (also known as 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul'), a foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author is Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi (d. 482 AH). The edition includes the hadith takhrij (source verification) by Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi (d. 802 AH). The text was edited by Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. This page provides bibliographic information and does not contain any legal rulings or discussions. It serves as an introduction to the book.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Uṣūl al-Bazdawī): The title of a famous Hanafi usul al-fiqh work by Imam al-Bazdawi.
كنز الوصول إلى معرفة الأصول (Kanz al-Wuṣūl ilā Maʿrifat al-Uṣūl): The full title of the book, meaning 'The Treasure of Arriving at Knowledge of the Principles'.
تخريج الأحاديث (Takhrij al-Aḥādīth): The process of tracing hadiths back to their original sources and verifying their authenticity.

Usul al-Bazdawi, authored by Imam al-Bazdawi, is a pivotal Hanafi usul al-fiqh text, and this edition includes the hadith takhrij of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Two Types of Knowledge and the Foundation of Creed
Author outlines two branches of knowledge and the foundation of creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of knowledge according to Al-Bazdawi and explain why the science of tawhid and attributes is foundational for usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Knowledge is divided into tawhid (creed) and fiqh (law); sound creed is the foundation of legal methodology.

This opening passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh establishes the framework for the entire work. The author distinguishes between two fundamental types of knowledge: the knowledge of divine unity and attributes (tawhid), and the knowledge of rulings and laws (fiqh). He emphasizes that the first type, tawhid, must be grounded in the Qur'an, Sunnah, and the path of the Salaf, avoiding innovation. This sets the stage for usul al-fiqh, which derives legal rulings from primary sources, but only after sound creed is established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Locate the sentence where Al-Bazdawi says 'العلم نوعان' and identify the two categories he mentions.
The two types are علم التوحيد والصفات and علم الفقه والشرائع والأحكام.
2
Determine the foundation of the first type
Read what Al-Bazdawi says is the 'أصل' (foundation) of the science of tawhid. Look for words like 'التمسك بالكتاب والسنة'.
The foundation is adherence to the Book and Sunnah, avoiding desires and innovation, and following the path of Ahl al-Sunnah.
3
Note the Hanafi authorities mentioned
Identify the scholars Al-Bazdawi cites as being upon this foundation: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
He also mentions that Abu Hanifa authored 'Al-Fiqh al-Akbar' on these matters.
4
Relate to usul al-fiqh
Consider why Al-Bazdawi begins his usul work with this discussion. How does tawhid serve as a prerequisite for legal methodology?
Sound creed ensures that the derivation of rulings is based on correct beliefs about Allah and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله خالقِ النَّسَم، ورازقِ القِسم مُبدع البدائع، وشارع الشرائع، دِيناً رَضِيَّاً، ونوراً مُضيَّاً، وذكراً للأنام، ومَطيَّةً إلى دار السلام. أحمده على الوسع والإمكان وأستعينه على طلب الرضوان، ونيل أسباب الغفران.
وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، وأصلي عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وعلى الأنبياء والمرسلين وأصحابهم أجمعين.
قال الشيخ الإمامُ الأجلَّ الزاهد أبو الحسن علي بن محمد البزدوي رحمه الله :
العلم :نوعان علم التوحيد والصفات، وعلم الفقه والشرائع والأحكام. والأصل في النوع الأول: هو التمسك بالكتاب والسنة، ومجانبة الهوى والبدعة، ولزوم طريق السنة والجماعة الذي كان عليه الصحابة والتابعون ومضى عليه الصالحون، وهو الذي أدركنا عليه مشايخنا الله ، وكان على ذلك سَلَفنا، أعني أبا حنيفة وأبا يوسف ومحمداً، رحمهم الله وعامة أصحابهم رضي عنهم. وقد صنف أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه في ذلك كتاب: «الفقه الأكبر»، وذَكَرَ فيه إثبات الصفات وإثبات تقدير الخير والشر من الله عزّ وجلَّ، وأن ذلك كله بمشيئته.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, the Creator of souls, the Provider of sustenance, the Originator of wonders, the Legislator of laws, a religion pleasing, a light shining, a remembrance for mankind, and a means to the abode of peace. I praise Him for ease and ability, and I seek His help to seek His pleasure and attain the means of forgiveness. And I bear witness that there is no deity but Allah alone, with no partner, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger. And I send blessings upon him, his family, his companions, and upon all the prophets and messengers and their companions, all of them. The Shaykh, the great Imam, the ascetic, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Knowledge is of two types: the knowledge of tawhid and the attributes, and the knowledge of fiqh, laws, and rulings. The foundation of the first type is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah, avoiding desires and innovation, and adhering to the path of the Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, which the Companions and the Followers were upon and which the righteous predecessors followed. This is what we found our teachers upon, and our predecessors—namely Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them and all their companions—were upon that. And Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, authored a book on that: 'Al-Fiqh al-Akbar,' in which he mentioned the affirmation of the attributes and the affirmation of the decree of good and evil from Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and that all of that is by His will.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is from the opening of Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh. The author begins with the basmalah, praise, and salutation, as is customary. He then states that knowledge is of two types: 1) the science of tawhid (divine unity) and the attributes of Allah, and 2) the science of fiqh, which deals with laws and rulings. This division is standard in Islamic scholarship, as creedal matters precede legal ones. Al-Bazdawi explains that the foundation of the first type (tawhid) is adherence to the Qur'an and Sunnah, avoiding personal desires (hawa) and innovations (bid'ah), and adhering to the path of the Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah as followed by the Companions and the righteous predecessors. He notes that this is the way of his teachers and the founders of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. He mentions that Abu Hanifa authored a work on this subject titled 'Al-Fiqh al-Akbar,' which affirms the divine attributes and the decree (qadar) of good and evil from Allah, and that everything occurs by His will. This sets the stage for the rest of the book, which will focus on usul al-fiqh, but here the author emphasizes the importance of sound creed as the basis for legal methodology.

Key Terms
الفقه الأكبر (al-fiqh al-akbar): A book by Abu Hanifa on creedal matters (tawhid and attributes), affirming the divine attributes and the decree of good and evil.
علم التوحيد والصفات (ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat): The science of divine unity and attributes, i.e., theology (kalam) and creed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, what is the foundation (أصل) of the science of tawhid and attributes?
A) Rational argument and philosophical speculation
B) The consensus of the later scholars
C) Adherence to the Book and Sunnah, avoiding innovation
D) The writings of the Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is built on the foundation of sound creed as defined by the Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Two Types of Knowledge and the Hanafi Creedal Foundation
Author distinguishes knowledge types and Hanafi creed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of knowledge according to al-Bazdawi and identify at least three Hanafi creedal positions affirmed in the passage.

Core Idea
Hanafi jurisprudence is built upon a firm creedal foundation: tawhid and rejection of innovation.

Imam al-Bazdawi opens his work on usul al-fiqh by dividing knowledge into two categories: theology (tawhid and attributes) and jurisprudence (fiqh and rulings). He then grounds the Hanafi school in a set of creedal principles derived from the Quran and Sunnah, emphasizing that the school's jurisprudential method is inseparable from its theological orthodoxy. This lesson will help you internalize that foundation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Locate the sentence where al-Bazdawi explicitly states the division of knowledge. Note the Arabic terms: 'ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat and 'ilm al-fiqh wa al-shara'i' wa al-ahkam.
This is the central structural claim of the passage.
2
Extract the foundation of the first type (tawhid)
Read the sentence that begins 'wa al-asl fi al-naw' al-awwal...' and list its components: adherence to Quran and Sunnah, avoidance of desire and innovation, and following the way of the Salaf.
This shows that Hanafi theology is methodologically conservative.
3
List the Hanafi creedal positions mentioned
Scan for specific doctrines attributed to Abu Hanifa and his students. Write down: affirmation of divine attributes and predestination, capacity with the act, creation of actions by Allah, rejection of al-aslah, no takfir due to sin, uncreatedness of the Quran, beatific vision, punishment of the grave, and creation of Paradise and Hell.
These positions distinguish Hanafis from Mu'tazila and other groups.
4
Recognize the authorities cited
Identify the three founding imams named: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note that Abu Hanifa authored theological works (al-Fiqh al-Akbar, etc.) and that Abu Yusuf debated him on khalq al-Qur'an.
This establishes the school's chain of authority.
5
Understand the transition to fiqh
Notice the closing sentence: 'The second type is the science of branches, which is Fiqh, and it is of three divisions.' This signals that the usul discussion will follow after this creedal preface.
The preface sets the theological context for the jurisprudential method to come.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله خالقِ النَّسَم، ورازقِ القِسم مُبدع البدائع، وشارع الشرائع، دِيناً رَضِيَّاً، ونوراً مُضيَّاً، وذكراً للأنام، ومَطيَّةً إلى دار السلام. أحمده على الوسع والإمكان وأستعينه على طلب الرضوان، ونيل أسباب الغفران.
وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، وأصلي عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وعلى الأنبياء والمرسلين وأصحابهم أجمعين.
قال الشيخ الإمامُ الأجلَّ الزاهد أبو الحسن علي بن محمد البزدوي رحمه الله : العلم :نوعان علم التوحيد والصفات، وعلم الفقه والشرائع والأحكام. والأصل في النوع الأول: هو التمسك بالكتاب والسنة، ومجانبة الهوى والبدعة، ولزوم طريق السنة والجماعة الذي كان عليه الصحابة والتابعون ومضى عليه الصالحون، وهو الذي أدركنا عليه مشايخنا، وكان على ذلك سَلَفنا، أعني أبا حنيفة وأبا يوسف ومحمداً، رحمهم الله وعامة أصحابهم رضي عنهم. وقد صنف أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه في ذلك كتاب: «الفقه الأكبر»، وذَكَرَ فيه إثبات الصفات وإثبات تقدير الخير والشر من الله عزّ وجلَّ، وأن ذلك كله بمشيئته. وأثبت الاستطاعة مع الفعل، وأن أفعال العباد مخلوقة بخلق الله تعالى إياها كلَّها، وردَّ القولَ بالأصلح. وصنف كتاب: العالم والمتعلم، وكتاب: «الرسالة»، وقال فيه: لا يُكفَرُ أحد بذنب، ولا يخرج به من الإيمان، ويُترحم له. وكان في علم الأصول إماماً صادقاً.
وقد صح عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله أنه قال: ناظرتُ أبا حنيفة في مسألة خَلْقِ القرآن ستة أشهر، فاتفق رأيي ورأيه على أن من قال بخلق القرآن : فهو كافر.
وقد صح هذا القول عن محمد رحمه الله.
ودلَّت المسائلُ المتفرّقةُ عن أصحابنا في المبسوط وغير المبسوط على أنهم لم يميلوا إلى شيء من مذاهب الاعتزال، وإلى سائر الأهواء. وإنهم قالوا بحَقِّية رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار في الدار الآخرة. وحقية عذاب القبر لمن شاء. وحقية خلق الجنة والنار، حتى قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله لجهم: أخرج عني يا كافر. وقالوا بحَقِّية سائر أحكام الآخرة على ما نَطَق به الكتاب والسنة.
وهذا فصل يطول تعداده.
والنوع الثاني : علم الفروع ، وهو الفقه، وهو ثلاثة أقسام:
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, the Creator of breaths, the Provider of sustenance, the Originator of wonders, the Legislator of laws, a religion pleasing, a light shining, a remembrance for mankind, and a mount to the abode of peace. I praise Him for the capacity and ability, and I seek His help in seeking pleasure and attaining the means of forgiveness. And I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner with Him, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger. I send blessings upon him, his family and companions, and upon all prophets and messengers and their companions. The Shaykh, the great Imam, the ascetic Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi—may Allah have mercy on him—said: Knowledge is of two types: knowledge of Tawhid and the attributes, and knowledge of Fiqh, sacred laws, and rulings. The foundation of the first type is adherence to the Book and Sunnah, avoidance of desire and innovation, and adherence to the way of the Sunnah and the community (Jama'ah) which was the practice of the Companions, the Followers, and the righteous who passed away, and which we found our shaykhs upon, and upon which our predecessors—meaning Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad—may Allah have mercy on them and all their companions, may Allah be pleased with them—were. And Abu Hanifa—may Allah be pleased with him—authored a book on that subject: 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar', in which he mentioned the affirmation of attributes, the affirmation of predestination of good and evil from Allah Almighty, and that all of that is by His will. And he affirmed capacity with the act, and that the actions of servants are created by Allah's creation of them all, and he rejected the doctrine of the most beneficial (al-aslah). And he authored the book 'al-Alim wa al-Muta'allim' and the book 'al-Risala', and said in it: 'No one is declared an unbeliever due to a sin, nor does he leave faith thereby, and mercy is sought for him.' And he was a truthful Imam in the science of principles. And it is authentically reported from Abu Yusuf—may Allah have mercy on him—that he said: 'I debated with Abu Hanifa on the issue of the creation of the Qur'an for six months, and my view and his view agreed that whoever says the Qur'an is created is an unbeliever.' And this statement is authentically reported from Muhammad—may Allah have mercy on him. And the scattered issues from our companions in al-Mabsut and other works indicate that they did not incline to any of the doctrines of Mu'tazilism or other desires. And they affirmed the reality of seeing Allah Almighty with the eyes in the Hereafter, and the reality of the punishment of the grave for whom He wills, and the reality of the creation of Paradise and Hell, so much so that Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on him—said to Jahm: 'Get away from me, O unbeliever.' And they affirmed the reality of all other rulings of the Hereafter as stated in the Book and Sunnah. This is a chapter whose enumeration would be lengthy. The second type is the science of branches, which is Fiqh, and it is of three divisions:
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Imam al-Bazdawi's work on usul al-fiqh. It is a preface that establishes the framework of knowledge as twofold: theology (tawhid and attributes) and jurisprudence (fiqh and rulings). The author emphasizes that the foundation of theology is strict adherence to Quran and Sunnah, avoidance of innovation, and following the path of the pious predecessors. He specifically names the three founding imams of the Hanafi school—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—and mentions Abu Hanifa's theological works: al-Fiqh al-Akbar, al-Alim wa al-Muta'allim, and al-Risala. The text then outlines key Hanafi creedal positions: affirmation of divine attributes and predestination, capacity with the act (as opposed to the Mu'tazili view of capacity before the act), that actions are created by Allah, rejection of the doctrine of the most beneficial (al-aslah), and rejection of takfir due to sin. A central issue is the creation of the Qur'an: Abu Hanifa and his students declared that whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever. The passage further affirms the Hanafi stance on beatific vision, punishment of the grave, and the creation of Paradise and Hell, all based on the Qur'an and Sunnah. The author then transitions to the second type of knowledge, fiqh, stating it has three divisions (to be explained). This introduction serves to establish the theological orthodoxy of the Hanafi school before delving into the principles of jurisprudence.

Key Terms
علم التوحيد والصفات (‘ilm al-tawhid wa al-sifat): Knowledge of the oneness of Allah and His attributes, i.e., theology.
الاستطاعة مع الفعل (al-istita‘ah ma‘a al-fi‘l): Capacity to act is simultaneous with the act itself, not prior.
خلق القرآن (khalq al-Qur’an): The doctrine that the Qur'an is created. Hanafis declare its proponents as disbelievers.
رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار (ru’yat Allah ta‘ala bi al-absar): Seeing Allah with the eyes in the Hereafter.
عذاب القبر (‘adhab al-qabr): Punishment of the grave for sinners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Bazdawi, what are the two types of knowledge?
A) Knowledge of fiqh and knowledge of hadith
B) Knowledge of tawhid and attributes, and knowledge of fiqh, sacred laws, and rulings
C) Knowledge of usul and knowledge of furu
D) Knowledge of the Quran and knowledge of the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Hanafi jurisprudence is grounded in a specific theological creed that affirms divine attributes, predestination, and the uncreatedness of the Qur'an, distinguishing it from Mu'tazilism.

Introduction and Front Matter

Hanafi Usul Methodology: The Integration of Hadith and Ra'y
Author praises Hanafi school and outlines its methodological principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three sources of Sharia and explain how the Hanafi school validates mursal hadith and ra'y as part of its usul methodology.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school integrates both hadith and reasoned understanding (ra'y) as complementary sources of law.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul opens the work by praising the Hanafi scholars as masters of both hadith and meaning. It defends the school's reliance on ra'y (juristic opinion) as a disciplined form of fiqh, and lists several methodological principles that distinguish the Hanafi approach. Read on to understand how the school balances textual sources and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cited hadith
Find the hadith 'إذا أراد الله بعبد خيراً يفقهه في الدين' and note its role: it establishes the virtue of understanding religion, which is the basis for the Hanafi emphasis on fiqh.
This hadith is a key proof for the importance of juristic reasoning.
2
Understand 'as-hab al-ra'y'
The author redefines 'ra'y' as 'اسمٌ للفقه الذي ذكرنا' – a name for deep fiqh, not arbitrary opinion. This defends the Hanafi school from the criticism of relying on subjective opinion.
Other schools sometimes use 'ra'y' pejoratively, but here it is a technical term.
3
List the three sources of Sharia
At the end, the author states: 'اعلم أن أصول الشرع ثلاثة: الكتاب والسنة والإجماع'. Identify these as the foundational sources.
Note that qiyas is not listed here but is introduced later in the work.
4
Extract the methodological principles
From the middle of the passage, list four distinct Hanafi principles: (1) permitting abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah, (2) acting upon mursal hadith, (3) preferring the narration of an unknown narrator over qiyas, (4) preferring the saying of a Companion over qiyas.
These principles show the high regard for transmitted texts even when weak.
5
Analyze the interdependence of hadith and ra'y
Read Imam Muhammad's statement: 'الحديث لا يستقيم إلا بالرأي، ولا يستقيم الرأي إلا بالحديث'. Understand that a jurist must master both; one without the other is insufficient for qada and fatwa.
This refutes the misconception that Hanafis neglect hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسلام إذا فقهوا (1)
وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إذا أراد الله بعبد خيراً : يُفقهه الدين (۲).
وأصحابنا رحمهم الله هم السابقون في هذا الباب، ولهم الرتبةُ العليا، والدرجة القصوى في علم الشريعة وهم الربانيون في علم الكتاب والسنة، وملازمة القدوة. وهم أصحاب الحديث والمعاني.
أما المعاني: فقد سلم لهم العلماء، حتى سموهم: أصحاب الرأي، والرأي: اسمٌ للفقه الذي ذكرنا.
وهم أولى بالحديث أيضاً، ألا يُرى أنهم جوزوا نسخ الكتاب بالسُّنَّة ؛ لقوة منزلة السنة عندهم. وعملوا بالمراسيل ؛ تمسكاً بالسنة والحديث، ورأوا العمل به مع الإرسال : أولى من العمل بالرأي.
ومن ردَّ المراسيل : فقد ردَّ كثيراً من السنة، وعمل بالفروع بتعطيل الأصول.
وقدموا رواية المجهول على القياس.
وقدَّموا قول الصحابي على القياس.
وقال محمد رحمه الله تعالى في كتاب أدب القاضي: الحديث لا يستقيم إلا بالرأي، ولا يستقيم الرأي إلا بالحديث، حتى إنَّ مَن لا يُحسن الحديث، أو علم الحديث، ولا يُحسِنُ الرأي: قال: لا يصلح للقضاء والفتوى.
وقد مَلاً كتبه من الحديث.
ومَن استراح بظاهر الحديث عن بحث المعاني، ونكل عن ترتيب الفروع على الأصول : انتسب إلى ظاهر الحديث.
وهذا الكتاب لبيان النصوص بمعانيها ، وتعريف الأصول بفروعها، على شرط الإيجاز والاختصار إن شاء الله تعالى، وما توفيقي إلا بالله عليه توكلت وإليه أنيب حسبنا الله ونعم الوكيل.
اعلم أن أصول الشرع ثلاثة : الكتابُ والسُّنَّة، والإجماع.
Islam when they understood (1). And he, peace be upon him, said: 'If Allah wants good for a servant, He gives him understanding of the religion (2).' And our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, are the foremost in this chapter, and they have the highest rank and the utmost degree in the knowledge of Sharia, and they are the rabbanites in the knowledge of the Book and the Sunnah, and they adhere to the example. And they are the people of hadith and meaning. As for meaning: the scholars have conceded to them, so much so that they called them the people of opinion, and opinion is a name for the fiqh that we mentioned. And they are also most entitled to hadith, do you not see that they permitted the abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah due to the strength of the status of the Sunnah with them. And they acted upon mursal hadith, adhering to the Sunnah and hadith, and they considered acting upon it despite its being mursal as preferable to acting upon opinion. And whoever rejects mursal hadith has rejected much of the Sunnah, and has acted upon subsidiary matters by disabling the principles. And they gave precedence to the narration of an unknown person over qiyas. And they gave precedence to the saying of a companion over qiyas. And Muhammad, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him, said in the book Adab al-Qadi: Hadith is not sound except with opinion, and opinion is not sound except with hadith, so much so that whoever is not proficient in hadith or the knowledge of hadith, and is not proficient in opinion, he said: he is not fit for qada and fatwa. And he filled his books with hadith. And whoever is content with the apparent meaning of hadith without investigating the meanings, and refrains from arranging branches upon principles, is attributed to the external meaning of hadith. And this book is for explaining the texts with their meanings, and defining the principles with their branches, on the condition of brevity and conciseness, Allah willing. And my success is only with Allah; upon Him I rely and to Him I turn. Sufficient for us is Allah, and He is the best trustee. Know that the sources of the Sharia are three: the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an introductory front matter from Al-Bazdawi's Usul, where the author establishes the credentials of the Hanafi school. He begins by citing two hadiths: one about the virtue of understanding religion and the other about the best of people being those who have understanding. He then praises the Hanafi scholars as the foremost in this field, calling them the 'people of hadith and meaning' (أصحاب الحديث والمعاني). This indicates that the Hanafi school is rooted both in transmitted texts and in reasoned understanding. The author emphasizes that the Hanafis are called 'people of opinion' (أصحاب الرأي) not as a criticism, but because their ra'y is actually deep fiqh grounded in the sources. He then lists several distinctive methodological principles: they permit abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah (a specific Hanafi position), they work with mursal hadith, they prioritize the narration of an unknown narrator over qiyas, and they prefer the saying of a Companion over qiyas. The author quotes Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, affirming that hadith and ra'y are interdependent: one cannot be a qualified judge or mufti without mastery of both. The passage concludes by stating the purpose of the book: to explain texts with their meanings and to define usul through their furu', and it ends with a summary of the three sources of Sharia: the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. This sets the stage for the usul work that follows.

Key Terms
فقه (fiqh): In this passage, it refers to deep understanding of the religion as praised in the hadith.
أصول الشرع (usul al-shar'): The three foundational sources of Islamic law: the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, and Ijma (consensus).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following did the Hanafi scholars give precedence over qiyas?
A) Quran and Sunnah
B) Mursal hadith and the saying of a companion
C) Consensus and analogy
D) The narration of an unknown narrator and the saying of a companion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is not anti-hadith; it integrates hadith and ra'y, giving precedence to transmitted narrations over qiyas and accepting mursal hadith to preserve the Sunnah.

Introduction and Front Matter

Causes of Shariah Rulings Are Signs, Not Obligators
Opens chapter explaining that Shariah rulings are caused by divinely ordained reasons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Shariah causes do not create obligation and state the Hanafi proof from ijma that obligation exists even when the divine address is absent.

Core Idea
Shariah causes merely indicate rulings; obligation is solely from Allah's command.

This chapter introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi legal theory: the causes (asbab) associated with Shariah rulings are not efficient causes. They are legislated signs placed to ease the servants' compliance. The real source of obligation is Allah's making obligatory (ijab), which is unseen. This principle is proven by consensus that a sleeping person is obligated to pray within the prayer time despite not being addressed.

Guided Path
1
Define the Concept of Asbab
Identify what the author means by 'causes' (asbab) of Shariah rulings. They are legislated associations placed to ease the servants, not efficient causes.
The term 'asbab' in Hanafi usul refers to indicators (amarat), not active causes.
2
Identify the Central Principle
Understand that the author clarifies obligation (wujub) is from Allah's command alone; the cause has no effect in creating obligation.
The cause is merely a sign that the ruling is now applicable.
3
Examine the Proof from Ijma
The author cites consensus on the obligation of prayer upon a sleeping person during the prayer time, even though the address (khitab) is removed from him. This shows obligation can exist without direct address.
The sleeping person is not addressed while asleep, but he is still obligated to pray.
4
Understand the Analogy with Sale
The author compares the command for performance to a sale: just as the sale necessitates the price, the command necessitates obligation, but the act of performance is demanded afterward.
This illustrates that obligation (wujub) is established by the initial command, not by the performance.
5
Distinguish Between Obligation and Address
Note that obligation can exist without the immediate address (e.g., for the sleeping, insane, and unconscious persons in certain conditions). This disproves any notion that causes themselves create obligation.
The insane person whose insanity ends within a day must pray, even though at the time of the prayer he was not addressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب بيان أسباب الشرائع
اعلم أن الأمر والنهي على الأقسام التي ذكرناها إنما يُراد بها طلب الأحكام المشروعة وأداؤها، وإنما الخطاب للأداء.
=
ولهذه الأحكام أسباب تضاف إليها شرعية، وضعت تيسيراً على العباد، وإنما الوجوب بإيجاب الله تعالى لا أثر للأسباب في ذلك، وإنما وضعت تيسيراً على العباد.
ولما كان الإيجاب غيباً عنا : نُسب الوجوب إلى الأسباب الموضوعة، وثبت الوجوب جبراً، لا اختيار للعبد فيه.
ثم الخطاب بالأمر والنهي للأداء بمنزلة البيع، يجب به الثمن، ثم يطالب بالأداء.

عليهما بالإجماع.
Chapter on the Explanation of the Causes of the Laws
Know that command and prohibition, in the categories we have mentioned, are intended only to request the legislated rulings and their performance, and the address is only for performance.
= 
And these rulings have causes added to them legislatively, placed as an ease for the servants, and obligation is only by Allah's making obligatory; the causes have no effect in that, and they are placed only as an ease for the servants.
And since the making obligatory is unseen to us, the obligation is attributed to the placed causes, and the obligation is established compulsorily, with no choice for the servant in it.
Then the address with command and prohibition for performance is like a sale: by it the price becomes obligatory, then one is demanded to pay.
And the evidence for the correctness of this principle is their consensus on the obligation of prayer upon the sleeping person during the time of prayer, while the address is removed from him.
And the obligation of prayer upon the insane person if his insanity ends within a day, and upon the unconscious person likewise, while the address is removed from both.
And likewise, insanity if it does not encompass the entire month of Ramadan.
And unconsciousness and sleep, even if they encompass it, do not prevent obligation, and there is no address upon them by consensus.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a new chapter on the causes (asbab) of Shariah rulings. The author explains that commands and prohibitions are addressed to people for the purpose of performing the rulings. Rulings have divinely appointed causes, but these causes do not actually create the obligation; they are merely means to make things easier for servants. The real source of obligation is Allah's command. Since Allah's making obligatory is unseen, we attribute the obligation to the apparent causes. Obligation is compulsory with no room for choice. The author draws an analogy: the command to perform is like a sale that makes the price obligatory, then the buyer is demanded to pay. The proof of this principle is the consensus (ijma) that prayer is obligatory on a sleeping person during the prayer time even though the address (the command to pray) is not directed to him (since he is asleep). Similarly, an insane person whose insanity ends within a day must pray, and an unconscious person, even though they are not addressed. Also, insanity that does not cover the entire month of Ramadan still obligates fasting. Sleep and unconsciousness, even if continuous, do not remove the obligation of prayer, by consensus.

Key Terms
أسباب الشرائع (asbab al-sharai'): The legislated causes that are associated with rulings to indicate their presence, such as time for prayer, but do not create obligation
وجوب (wujub): The legal quality of being obligatory; the obligation itself
خطاب (khitab): The divine address (command or prohibition) directed to the legally responsible person

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The obligation of a sale to pay the price.
C) The obligation of fasting on a traveler.
D) The obligation of zakat on the rich.

Key Takeaway
Shariah causes are merely legislated signs; obligation arises solely from Allah's command, as proven by the consensus that a sleeping person is obligated to pray despite not being addressed.

Introduction and Front Matter

Overview of the Hanafi Usul Bibliography
Listing references and editions cited in the work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize the major works in this bibliography by genre and explain their relevance to Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A scholar's bibliography reveals the living tradition of commentary, critique, and biographical grounding that shapes Hanafi usul.

This passage presents a list of works cited in the critical edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul. At first glance, it may appear to be a mere collection of titles, but it actually maps the scholarly ecosystem of Hanafi usul: commentaries that refine the text, hadith works that verify the proofs, and biographical dictionaries that trace the chain of transmission. Learning to read such a bibliography is a key skill for any serious student of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bibliography's scope
Notice that the list includes works of usul (e.g., al-Taqrir, Tanqih al-Usul), hadith (Sunan al-Bayhaqi), history (Tarikh Dimashq), and biography (Taj al-Tarajim, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah). This diversity shows that Hanafi usul draws on multiple disciplines.
The bibliography is not exhaustive but representative of the editor's sources.
2
Categorize each entry by genre
Go through the list and assign each work a primary category: usul commentary, usul textbook, hadith collection, biographical work, historical chronicle, or general reference (e.g., Taj al-'Arus).
Use the title and author's specialization to decide. For example, al-Bayhaqi is a hadith scholar, so his Sunan is a hadith source.
3
Identify works directly related to al-Bazdawi's Usul
Look for entries that explicitly mention 'Usul al-Bazdawi' or are known commentaries: al-Taqrir Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi, Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi, and Tanqih al-Usul (which is a later compendium based on al-Bazdawi). These form the immediate commentarial tradition.
Tanqih al-Usul by Sadr al-Shari'ah is itself a text that was commented upon, but it builds on al-Bazdawi.
4
Note the edition information
Each entry includes the editor, publisher, and date. This helps determine the reliability and availability of the edition. For example, al-Taqrir was edited by Dr. 'Abd al-Salam Subhi Salih and published by the Kuwaiti Ministry of Awqaf, a reputable source.
Photostat editions (e.g., for al-Ansab) indicate that the work was reproduced from an earlier print.
5
Summarize the supporting role of non-usul works
Works like Hilyat al-Awliya' and al-Jami' li Akhlaq al-Rawi provide biographical and ethical context for hadith transmitters, which is essential for evaluating hadith proofs in usul. Similarly, Tarikh Dimashq supplies historical background for early scholars.
This shows that usul is not an isolated discipline; it relies on auxiliary sciences.

This passage is a bibliography or list of primary and secondary sources cited in the edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul. Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition or scholarly editing of a manuscript.
ط (tab'a): Edition or printing of a book.
شرح (sharh): Commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
تخريج (takhrij): The science of tracing hadith to their original sources and evaluating their chains.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Commentaries on al-Bazdawi's Usul
Listing references and editions cited in the work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a sharh, a takhrij, and a hashiya, and identify the specific works that form the commentarial tradition of al-Bazdawi's Usul.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi's Usul generated a rich commentarial tradition that refines, defends, and applies his principles.

The bibliography includes several works that directly engage with al-Bazdawi's text: al-Taqrir (a sharh by al-Babarti), Takhrij Ahadith (a hadith extraction by Qutlubugha), and Tanqih al-Usul (an independent reworking by Sadr al-Shari'ah). These works represent different facets of the commentarial enterprise. Understanding what each type does is crucial for navigating the secondary literature of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the direct commentaries on al-Bazdawi
From the list, pick out entries that explicitly mention 'Usul al-Bazdawi' in the title: al-Taqrir Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi and Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi. Also note that Tanqih al-Usul, while not directly titled as such, is heavily based on al-Bazdawi.
Al-Taqrir is a straightforward sharh; Takhrij focuses only on hadith.
2
Define the genre of each work
Al-Taqrir is a sharh (line-by-line commentary) that explains al-Bazdawi's arguments. Takhrij Ahadith is a takhrij work that extracts and verifies the hadith proofs. Tanqih al-Usul is a new matn that reorganizes and condenses usul principles, drawing from al-Bazdawi and others.
Sharh and takhrij serve different purposes: one clarifies reasoning, the other authenticates evidence.
3
Analyze the relationship between Tanqih and al-Bazdawi
Tanqih al-Usul by Sadr al-Shari'ah is a later work that refines al-Bazdawi's system. It itself has commentaries (al-Tawdih) and supercommentaries (al-Talwih). This shows a lineage of texts building upon each other.
Tanqih is not a direct commentary but a derivative textual tradition.
4
Identify the hashiya tradition
Hashiyat Ibn 'Abidin (Radd al-Muhtar) is a later hashiya (gloss) on the Hanafi fiqh text al-Durr al-Mukhtar, but it also reflects usul principles. It shows how usul commentaries feed into fiqh works.
Though not directly on al-Bazdawi, it is part of the broader Hanafi commentarial tradition.
5
Summarize the chain of transmission
The bibliography shows a chain: al-Bazdawi's matn → al-Taqrir (sharh) → Takhrij (hadith work) → Tanqih (new matn) → al-Tawdih (sharh on Tanqih) → al-Talwih (hashi on al-Tawdih). This illustrates how a single text can spawn multiple layers of commentary.
Each layer adds analysis, correction, or expansion.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography or list of primary and secondary sources cited in the edition of al-Bazdawi's Usul. It includes classical works of fiqh, hadith, history, biography, and usul al-fiqh, along with their editors and publication details. The list demonstrates the breadth of sources used by Hanafi scholars, including works by Ibn Hajar, al-Sam'ani, al-Baghdadi, al-Zubaydi, Ibn 'Asakir, al-Babarti, Sadr al-Shari'ah, al-Taftazani, al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, al-Qurashi, Ibn 'Abidin, Abu Nu'aym, al-Zayla'i, al-Sakhawi, and al-Bayhaqi. Many are standard references in Hanafi fiqh and usul. The inclusion of Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi and al-Taqrir shows direct engagement with al-Bazdawi's text.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): Commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
تخريج (takhrij): The science of tracing hadith to their original sources and evaluating their chains.
حاشية (hashiaya): Supercommentary or gloss that annotates a sharh or matn, often adding critical notes.
تنقيح (tanqih): Refinement or revision of a text or set of principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Al-Tawdih
C) Al-Talwih
D) Takhrij Ahadith

Key Takeaway
The commentarial tradition of al-Bazdawi's Usul demonstrates how a single matn can generate multiple layers of analysis—sharh (explanation), takhrij (hadith verification), and tanqih (refinement)—each serving a distinct scholarly purpose.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Navigating the Hanafi and Usul Bibliographic Landscape
Listing of reference works cited in the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify major Hanafi biographical and Usul works cited in classical editions.

Core Idea
A scholar's bibliography is a map of the tradition; knowing the sources is the first step in rigorous scholarship.

This passage is a typical bibliography from a scholarly edition of Usul al-Bazdawi. It lists works on Hanafi biography (tabaqat), usul commentaries, hadith, and general reference. Understanding these sources helps you navigate the Hanafi tradition and locate authoritative texts for your research.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main categories of works
Group the listed works into categories: Hanafi biographical dictionaries (al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, etc.), commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi (al-Kafi Sharh, Kashf al-Asrar), hadith works (Mushkil al-Athar, Ma'alim al-Sunan), and general reference (Kashf al-Zunun, Mu'jam al-Buldan).
This classification helps you quickly locate the type of source you need.
2
Note the authors and their dates
Record the names of the authors and their death dates (e.g., al-Sighnaqi d. 714 AH, al-Bukhari d. 730 AH). This helps you understand the chronological development of the Hanafi school.
Dates are crucial for evaluating the authority of a work (e.g., early vs. late commentaries).
3
Recognize direct commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi
Identify which works are direct commentaries or supercommentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi, such as al-Kafi Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi and Kashf al-Asrar. These are primary sources for understanding the text.
Knowing the commentary tradition helps you trace interpretations and tarjih (preferences).
4
Understand the role of Tabaqat works
Biographical dictionaries (Tabaqat) provide information about Hanafi scholars, their teachers, and their works. They are essential for verifying chains of transmission and understanding the context of rulings.
Works like al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya are key for Hanafi rijal studies.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography listing the sources cited in the edition of Usul al-Bazdawi. It contains 18 entries (from number 31 to 48) covering works on Hanafi biography (Tabaqat), principles of jurisprudence (Usul), Hadith, geography, and general reference. Many of these works are commentaries or supercommentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi itself, such as al-Kafi Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi by al-Sighnaqi and Kashf al-Asrar by al-Bukhari. The list also includes biographical dictionaries of Hanafi scholars like al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, as well as standard reference works like Kashf al-Zunun and Mu'jam al-Buldan. This bibliography is a typical feature of scholarly editions to document the sources used for verification and cross-referencing.

Key Terms
شرح أصول البزدوي (Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi): A commentary on the foundational Hanafi usul work by al-Bazdawi. Two examples are al-Kafi and Kashf al-Asrar.
تراجم الحنفية (Tarajim al-Hanafiyya): Biographical dictionaries of Hanafi scholars, such as al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya.

Introduction and Front Matter

Structure of Usul al-Bazdawi: Key Classifications in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Table of contents listing sections and page numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sources of Sharia and list the key categories of textual expressions (khass, amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal, etc.) as outlined in the table of contents of Usul al-Bazdawi.

Core Idea
The table of contents of Usul al-Bazdawi maps the essential categories of legal texts that form the foundation of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

This lesson introduces the structural outline of Imam al-Bazdawi's foundational work on Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Even a simple table of contents reveals the book's systematic approach: it begins by establishing the four sources of Sharia, then proceeds to dissect the types of textual expressions (specific, general, ambiguous, etc.) and their implications for deriving rulings. Understanding this roadmap will help you navigate the detailed discussions in subsequent lessons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sources of Sharia
Locate the statement 'أصول الشرع أربعة' in the text. List the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
2
Recognize the main categories of textual expression
Note the pairs listed: الخاص والعام والمشترك والمؤول, الظاهر والنص والمفسر والمحكم, الخفي والمشكل والمجمل والمتشابه, الحقيقة والمجاز والصريح والكناية, and the implications of the text (عبارة النص وإشارته ودلالته واقتضائه).
These categories are used to classify each legal text.
3
Understand the chapter sequence
Look at the chapters from باب بیان معرفة أحكام الخصوص to باب أحكام الحقيقة والمجاز والصريح والكناية. This shows a progression from specification to command to generality to interpretation.
The order reflects the logical flow: start with particular rulings, then commands, then general terms, then interpretation tools.
4
Appreciate the Hanafi emphasis on ra'y
The text mentions that Hanafis are called 'أصحاب الرأي' (people of opinion), meaning they rely on juristic reasoning. This sets the stage for their usul methodology.
This is a key distinction from other schools that may prioritize hadith over reasoning.

Source Text

Beginning of the book Usul al-Bazdawi. Beginning of the book Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi by Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha. Knowledge of fiqh has three divisions. Meaning of their saying: The Hanafis are the people of ra'y (opinion): i.e., the people of fiqh. The sources of Sharia are four: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. Divisions of wording and meaning, and speech in summary about: the specific, the general, and the ambiguous, and the interpreted, and the apparent, and the clear text, and the explained, and the decisive, and the hidden, and the problematic, and the vague, and the ambiguous, and the literal and metaphorical, and explicit and implicit, and the statement of the text, its indication, its implication, and its requirement. Chapter on the knowledge of rulings of specification. Chapter on command. Chapter on the import of command. Command after prohibition. Chapter on the import of command in the sense of generality and repetition. Chapter on the explanation of the ruling of command (performance and recompense). Chapter on the explanation of the goodness of the commanded thing. Chapter on the division of the commanded in terms of time (absolute and time-bound acts of worship). Chapter on prohibition. Chapter on knowledge of rulings of generality. Chapter on the general when specification applies to it. Chapter on words of generality. Chapter on knowledge of rulings of the section that follows: the apparent, the clear text, the explained, and the decisive. Chapter on rulings of literal and metaphorical, explicit and implicit.
Source pages p. 824

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihris) of the book 'Usul al-Bazdawi' by Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, along with the beginning of the takhrij (verification of hadiths) by Qasim bin Qutlubugha. It outlines the structure of the work. The book begins by stating that fiqh knowledge has three divisions, and that the Hanafis are called 'people of ra'y' because they are experts in fiqh (as opposed to mere hadith narrators). It then lists the four sources of Sharia: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. The author enumerates the categories of legal texts and meanings: specific (khass), general (amm), common (mushtarak), interpreted (mu’awwal), apparent (zahir), clear text (nass), explained (mufassar), decisive (muhkam), hidden (khafi), problematic (mushkil), vague (mujmal), ambiguous (mutashabih), literal (haqiqah), metaphorical (majaz), explicit (sarih), implicit (kinayah), and the implications of the text (ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida). The subsequent chapters are listed, covering topics such as specification, command and its implications, prohibition, generality, and the various textual categories. This front matter serves as a roadmap for the detailed discussions that follow in the book.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The title of the book, meaning 'The Fundamentals of al-Bazdawi', a famous Hanafi usul al-fiqh work by Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.
تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي (Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi): A commentary by Qasim bin Qutlubugha that traces the hadiths cited in Usul al-Bazdawi.
الخاص والعام والمشترك والمؤول (al-khass wa al-amm wa al-mushtarak wa al-mu’awwal): Categories of textual expressions: specific, general, common (ambiguous between meanings), and interpreted (remotely likely meaning after evidence).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The table of contents of Usul al-Bazdawi provides a roadmap for the key classifications in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, emphasizing the four sources and the types of textual expressions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Introduction to al-Bazdawi's Usul: The Hanafi Method and Foundational Sources
Introduces the book and lists all chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafis are called Ashab al-Ra'y and identify the four foundational sources of Islamic law according to al-Bazdawi.

Core Idea
The Hanafis are people of deep legal insight (fiqh), not arbitrary opinion, and the Shariah rests on four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.

Al-Bazdawi opens his Usul by clarifying a key term and stating the foundational sources. This sets the stage for the entire work. Understanding this reframing of 'ra'y' and the four usul is essential before diving into the detailed chapters on commands, prohibitions, and linguistic analysis.

Guided Path
1
Locate the meaning of Ashab al-Ra'y
Find where the author explains why Hanafis are called 'people of opinion'. Note that it is defined as 'people of fiqh' (deep understanding).
This refutes the misconception that Hanafis disregard texts.
2
Identify the four sources of Shariah
The passage states 'Usul al-Shar' are four: the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. Commit these to memory.
These are agreed upon by all major schools, though additional sources may be debated.
3
Preview the linguistic categories
Scan the list of topics: specific/general, apparent/explicit, literal/metaphorical, etc. This gives you the book's roadmap.
Each topic will be explained in later chapters.

Source pages p. 825

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh. It begins by explaining why the Hanafi madhhab is called 'Ashab al-Ra'y' (people of opinion): not because they rely on arbitrary opinion, but because they are the people of deep legal understanding (fiqh). Then it states the four foundational sources of Islamic law: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogical reasoning (qiyas). The author then presents an overview of the topics covered in the book, including: the divisions of wording and meaning such as specific (khass), general (amm), and shared (mushtarak); the categories of textual clarity (zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam) and ambiguity (khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih); and linguistic devices like literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz), explicit (sarih) and allusive (kinayah). Then follows a detailed table of contents listing all the chapters (abwab) of the book, covering commands, prohibitions, generality and specificity, particles, prepositions, and other key topics in usul al-fiqh. This serves as a roadmap for the reader.

Key Terms
أصحاب الرأي (Ashab al-Ra'y): The Hanafi school, called 'people of opinion' because of their extensive use of legal reasoning (ra'y) based on the sources, not on arbitrary opinion.
أصول الشرع (Usul al-Shar'): The four foundational sources of Islamic law: the Quran, Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They reject consensus and analogy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis are called Ashab al-Ra'y because of their deep fiqh, and the Shariah is built on four foundational sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.

Introduction and Front Matter

Overview of Usul al-Bazdawi: Structure and Purpose
List of chapter headings and topics covered in the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the structure of Usul al-Bazdawi and identify the major topics covered in each section.

Core Idea
The fihrist is a roadmap to Hanafi usul, covering linguistic analysis, hadith criticism, and legal theory.

This lesson introduces the fihrist (table of contents) of Usul al-Bazdawi, a foundational Hanafi usul text. The fihrist reveals the author's systematic approach: starting from linguistic principles, moving through hadith methodology, and concluding with ijtihad. Understanding this structure helps you locate specific rulings and appreciate the coherence of the Hanafi usul system.

Guided Path
1
Overview of the fihrist
Read the list of chapters and note the sequence. Recognize the three main clusters: linguistic analysis, hadith criticism, and legal theory.
2
Identify the three main sections
Group the chapters into: (1) Linguistic foundations (haqiqah, huruf, prepositions, etc.), (2) Textual indications and legal categories (ibarah, azimah, etc.), (3) Hadith criticism (mutawatir, narrator conditions, etc.).
3
Locate key terms
Find the chapters on haqiqah, huruf al-ma'ani, mutawatir, khabar al-wahid, and narrator conditions. These are central to Hanafi usul.
4
Relate to the overall usul methodology
See how the order reflects the Hanafi method: language first, then hadith, then legal derivation. This progression is deliberate.
